Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Praying Zuhr Before Jumu'ah
Explains the karahah of praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah for one without excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah as makruh rather than haram, and evaluate the proof from consensus.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah is disliked because it does not necessitate missing Jumu'ah; the sin is only in failing to attend.

When Friday arrives, a Muslim must attend the Jumu'ah prayer. But what if someone prays Zuhr before the Jumu'ah time begins? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling: it is disliked (makruh) but valid, and the real sin is skipping the Jumu'ah congregation. The commentator defends al-Quduri's wording against a claim from Fath al-Qadir that it is forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah for one without a valid excuse. The Hanafi ruling from al-Quduri is that it is makruh (disliked) but valid. Note that the prayer itself is not haram.
2
Understand the dispute about the ruling
The commentator discusses a view from Fath al-Qadir that it is haram. Identify why the Hanafi school rejects this: because simply praying Zuhr does not cause missing Jumu'ah; missing occurs only if one fails to proceed to the congregation.
The key is that proceeding to Jumu'ah after Zuhr is obligatory.
3
Locate the dalil used by the Hanafi school
The Hanafi school uses consensus (ijma) to prove that the obligation of the time (fard al-waqt) is Zuhr, not Jumu'ah. They argue that if one misses the Friday prayer, he makes up Zuhr, showing that Zuhr is the original obligation.
The dalil is ijma, which is qat'i in transmission.
4
Trace the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
The disagreement on fard al-waqt affects three issues: 1) this ruling (makruh vs. haram), 2) what one intends when entering prayer, 3) make-up rules when a missed prayer is remembered.
For example, if one intends 'fard al-waqt', according to Hanafi he intends Zuhr, according to Zufar he intends Jumu'ah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The relied-upon position is that of al-Quduri and Ibn Nujaym: the Zuhr is makruh and valid. The commentator confirms this and rejects the stronger prohibition claim.
This position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة الجمعة
أن يؤم فيها وتنعقد بهم ومن لا عذر له لو صلى الظهر قبلها كره فإن سعى إليها بطل
وقد قدمنا أن من أنكر فريضتها فهو كافر بالله تعالى. قال في فتح القدير: لا بد من كون المراد حرم عليه ذلك وصحت الظهر لأن ترك الفرض القطعي باتفاقهم الذي هو أكد من الظهر، فكيف لا يكون مرتكباً محرماً غير أن الظهر تقع صحيحة ا هـ . فالحاصل أن فرض الوقت هو الظهر عندنا بدلالة الإجماع على أن بخروج الوقت يصلي الظهر بنية القضاء، فلو لم يكن أصل فرض الوقت الظهر لما نوى القضاء. ثم هو مأمور بإسقاطه والإتيان بالجمعة. وعند زفر : فرض الوقت هو الجمعة وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في ثلاثة : أحدها في هذه المسألة. ثانيها لو نوى فرض الوقت يصير شارعاً في الظهر عندنا، وعنده في الجمعة. ثالثها لو تذكر فائتة عليه وكان لو اشتغل بالقضاء تفوته الجمعة دون الظهر فإنه يقضي ويصلي الظهر بعده عندنا، وعنده يصلي الجمعة ولو كان بحال تفوته الظهر والجمعة لا يقضيها اتفاقاً. كذا في أكثر الكتب. وفي المحيط ذكر ثلاثة أقوال عندهما فرض الوقت الظهر لكن العبد مأمور بإسقاطه عنه بأداء الجمعة، وعند محمد الفرض هو الجمعة وله أن يسقط بالظهر رخصة، وروي عنه الفرض أحدهما لا بعينه ويتعين ذلك بأدائه، وعند زفر والشافعي: الفرض هو الجمعة والظهر بدل عنها في حق المعذور ا هـ . وقد ظهر للعبد الضعيف صحة كلام القدوري ومن تبعه في التعبير بالكراهة لأن صلاة الظهر قبل أداء الجمعة من الإمام ليست مفوتة للجمعة حتى تكون حراماً إنما المفوت لها عدم سعيه، فإن سعيه بعد صلاة الظهر إليها فرض كما صرحوا به، فإن لم يسع فقد فوتها فحرم عليه ذلك وأما الصلاة فإنها مكروهة فقط باعتبار أنها قد تكون سبباً للتفويت باعتبار اعتماده عليها وهم إنم حكموا على صلاة الظهر بالكراهة ولم يقل أحد أن ترك الجمعة بغير عذر مكروه حتى يلزم ما ذكر من الإيقاع في جهالة. فقوله في فتح القدير لأنه ترك الفرض القطعي ممنوع لما علمت أنه لا يلزم من صلاة الظهر ترك الفرض والله سبحانه الموفق للصواب.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Friday Prayer. ... He should lead in it and it is valid with them. And whoever has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before it, it is disliked; if he proceeds to it, it becomes void. And we have already mentioned that whoever denies its obligation is a disbeliever in Allah Almighty. He said in Fath al-Qadir: It must be understood that [the meaning] is that it is forbidden for him and his Zuhr is valid, because he has abandoned the definitive obligation by their consensus which is stronger than Zuhr; how could it not be a prohibited act? However, the Zuhr is valid. So the conclusion is that the obligation of the time is Zuhr according to us, evidenced by consensus that when the time exits, he prays Zuhr with the intention of make-up. If the original obligation of the time were not Zuhr, he would not intend make-up. Then he is commanded to drop it and perform Jumu'ah. According to Zufar: the obligation of the time is Jumu'ah, and the benefit of the difference appears in three: one is this issue; second, if he intends the obligation of the time, he enters into Zuhr according to us, and according to him into Jumu'ah; third, if he remembers a missed prayer and if he occupied himself with make-up, Jumu'ah would be missed but not Zuhr, then according to us he makes up and prays Zuhr after it, and according to him he prays Jumu'ah. And if he were in a situation where both Zuhr and Jumu'ah are missed, he does not make up by consensus. Thus in most books. And in al-Muhit, three opinions are mentioned: according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the obligation of the time is Zuhr but the servant is commanded to drop it by performing Jumu'ah; according to Muhammad the obligation is Jumu'ah and he may drop it by Zuhr as a concession; and it is narrated from him that the obligation is one of them not specified, and it is determined by performing it; and according to Zufar and al-Shafi'i: the obligation is Jumu'ah and Zuhr is a substitute for it for the excused person. And it has become clear to the weak servant the correctness of the statement of al-Quduri and those who followed him in expressing it as dislike, because praying Zuhr before the Imam's performance of Jumu'ah does not cause missing Jumu'ah such that it would be prohibited; what causes missing is his not proceeding. Indeed, his proceeding to it after Zuhr is obligatory as they stated; if he does not proceed, he has missed it so that becomes prohibited for him. As for the prayer, it is only disliked because it may become a cause for missing due to his reliance on it. They only ruled the Zuhr prayer as disliked, and no one said that missing Jumu'ah without excuse is disliked such that the mentioned confusion would occur. So his statement in Fath al-Qadir that he has abandoned the definitive obligation is rejected, because as you know, praying Zuhr does not necessarily entail abandoning the obligation. And Allah Almighty is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the legal status of praying Zuhr before the Friday prayer for a person who has no valid excuse (like travel or illness). The core ruling from al-Quduri is that such a Zuhr prayer is makruh (disliked). The commentator (Ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) engages with a comment from Fath al-Qadir which suggests that the act is actually haram (forbidden) because it involves abandoning the definitive obligation of Jumu'ah. The commentator refutes this, arguing that simply performing Zuhr does not necessarily cause one to miss Jumu'ah; missing occurs only if one then fails to proceed to the Jumu'ah congregation. Since proceeding to Jumu'ah after Zuhr is obligatory (as clarified by the Hanafi school), the sin is only incurred if one neglects that obligation. Therefore, the Zuhr prayer itself is only makruh—not haram—because it may lead to missing Jumu'ah if one relies on it and does not go. The commentator supports this by noting that no scholar has ever said that missing Jumu'ah without excuse is merely makruh (it is haram), so the ruling cannot contradict that. Thus, the correct expression is karahah, not hurmah. The passage also briefly introduces the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute about whether the actual obligation of the time (fard al-waqt) is Zuhr or Jumu'ah, which affects the ruling's foundation.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): A legal classification meaning the act is disliked (makruh), but not forbidden (haram). In this context, praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah is makruh because it could lead to missing Jumu'ah.
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer that is specifically due for the current time period. In the Friday context, the dispute is whether it is Zuhr or Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing Zuhr prayer before the Friday prayer for a person without a valid excuse?
A) It is haram and invalid.
B) It is makruh but valid.
C) It is permissible and recommended.
D) It is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is disliked but valid; the sin is only in failing to attend Jumu'ah afterwards.

Dispute on the Obligatory Prayer of Time on Friday: Is it Zuhr or Jumu'ah?
Intra- and inter-madhhab dispute on fard al-waqt on Friday.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fard al-waqt on Friday and explain the practical consequences of the dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
The fard al-waqt on Friday is Zuhr, proven by consensus on qada; Jumu'ah replaces it for the community.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a key intra- and inter-madhhab dispute: what is the obligatory prayer of the time (fard al-waqt) on Friday? The Hanafi school, based on Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, holds that it is Zuhr, while Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i argue it is Jumu'ah. This difference has significant practical effects, especially regarding qada and intention. Let's trace the evidence and implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi position is that the fard al-waqt is Zuhr. The evidence is consensus (ijma) that when Friday time ends, one makes up Zuhr (qada), which shows Zuhr was the original obligation.
The text says 'bi dalalat al-ijma'.
2
Understand the opposing views
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold that Jumu'ah is the fard al-waqt, with Zuhr as a substitute for the excused. Also note Muhammad al-Shaybani's multiple narrations.
Muhammad's views include: Jumu'ah as fard, or indeterminate between the two.
3
Analyze the three practical consequences
The text lists three: (a) ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah, (b) what one enters when intending fard al-waqt, (c) precedence when a missed prayer is remembered during Jumu'ah time.
Each consequence differs based on whether fard al-waqt is Zuhr or Jumu'ah.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that fard al-waqt is Zuhr, per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and this is supported by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Muhammad's alternative views are not adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن فرض الوقت هو الظهر عندنا بدلالة الإجماع على أن بخروج الوقت يصلي الظهر بنية القضاء، فلو لم يكن أصل فرض الوقت الظهر لما نوى القضاء. ثم هو مأمور بإسقاطه والإتيان بالجمعة. وعند زفر : فرض الوقت هو الجمعة وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في ثلاثة : أحدها في هذه المسألة. ثانيها لو نوى فرض الوقت يصير شارعاً في الظهر عندنا، وعنده في الجمعة. ثالثها لو تذكر فائتة عليه وكان لو اشتغل بالقضاء تفوته الجمعة دون الظهر فإنه يقضي ويصلي الظهر بعده عندنا، وعنده يصلي الجمعة ولو كان بحال تفوته الظهر والجمعة لا يقضيها اتفاقاً. كذا في أكثر الكتب. وفي المحيط ذكر ثلاثة أقوال عندهما فرض الوقت الظهر لكن العبد مأمور بإسقاطه عنه بأداء الجمعة، وعند محمد الفرض هو الجمعة وله أن يسقط بالظهر رخصة، وروي عنه الفرض أحدهما لا بعينه ويتعين ذلك بأدائه، وعند زفر والشافعي: الفرض هو الجمعة والظهر بدل عنها في حق المعذور ا هـ .
So the conclusion is that the obligation of the time is Zuhr according to us, evidenced by consensus that when the time exits, he prays Zuhr with the intention of make-up. If the original obligation of the time were not Zuhr, he would not intend make-up. Then he is commanded to drop it and perform Jumu'ah. According to Zufar: the obligation of the time is Jumu'ah, and the benefit of the difference appears in three: one is this issue; second, if he intends the obligation of the time, he enters into Zuhr according to us, and according to him into Jumu'ah; third, if he remembers a missed prayer and if he occupied himself with make-up, Jumu'ah would be missed but not Zuhr, then according to us he makes up and prays Zuhr after it, and according to him he prays Jumu'ah. And if he were in a situation where both Zuhr and Jumu'ah are missed, he does not make up by consensus. Thus in most books. And in al-Muhit, three opinions are mentioned: according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the obligation of the time is Zuhr but the servant is commanded to drop it by performing Jumu'ah; according to Muhammad the obligation is Jumu'ah and he may drop it by Zuhr as a concession; and it is narrated from him that the obligation is one of them not specified, and it is determined by performing it; and according to Zufar and al-Shafi'i: the obligation is Jumu'ah and Zuhr is a substitute for it for the excused person.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a full inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute about what constitutes the obligatory prayer of the time (fard al-waqt) on Friday. The Hanafi school (based on Abu Hanifa and the majority) holds that the original obligation is Zuhr prayer, but the community is commanded to drop it by performing the Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). The proof is the consensus (ijma) that when the Friday time expires, one makes up the Zuhr prayer (qada), indicating its foundational status. Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that the actual obligation is Jumu'ah, and Zuhr is only a substitute for those with an excuse. The text then lists three practical consequences: (1) the ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah (if one holds fard al-waqt is Zuhr, it is a valid but disliked act; if Jumu'ah, it is invalid), (2) if one intends to pray the fard al-waqt, whether he enters Zuhr or Jumu'ah, and (3) if a missed prayer is remembered while Friday prayer is ongoing, whether one makes up the missed prayer and then prays Zuhr (Hanafi) or proceeds with Jumu'ah (Zufar). The text also notes an additional opinion from Muhammad al-Shaybani that the obligation is indeterminate between the two and is determined by performance. The purpose of detailing this dispute is to show that the ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah being makruh is consistent with the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer specifically tied to a particular time; on Friday, the dispute is whether it is Zuhr or Jumu'ah.
قضاء (qada): The make-up prayer performed after the time has elapsed; here used as evidence for the original obligation of Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference (thamarah) between the view that fard al-waqt is Zuhr and the view that it is Jumu'ah when a person remembers a missed prayer and is about to pray Zuhr?
A) According to the Hanafi view, he should make up the missed prayer and then pray Zuhr; according to Zufar, he should pray Jumu'ah.
B) According to the Hanafi view, he should proceed to Jumu'ah; according to Zufar, he should make up the missed prayer.
C) Both views agree that he should pray Jumu'ah.
D) Both views agree that he should pray Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
The fard al-waqt on Friday is Zuhr according to the Hanafi school, and this determines the ruling on qada and intention.

Nullification of Zuhr by Proceeding to Jumu'ah
Explains nullification of Zuhr by proceeding to Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when Zuhr becomes nullified upon proceeding to Jumu'ah, identify the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the conditions that affect nullification.

Core Idea
Zuhr is voided by merely leaving for Jumu'ah (Abu Hanifa); only joining the Imam voids it according to the Sahibayn.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) replaces the Zuhr prayer for those obligated. However, what happens if one has already prayed Zuhr and then decides to attend Jumu'ah? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the nullification of a performed Zuhr when one sets out to join the Friday congregation, based on the command in Surah al-Jumu'ah and the internal Hanafi discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (praying Zuhr and then proceeding to Jumu'ah) and the legal consequence (the Zuhr becomes batil).
The ruling is specific to Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn differ.
2
Locate the principal proof
Find the Quranic evidence cited (62:9) and understand how it implies nullification through the command to proceed.
The imperatival form 'fas'aw' is interpreted as walking, and the reasoning is that proceeding is the beginning of the commanded nullification.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view with that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, who require entering with the Imam for nullification.
The text also mentions Zufar and al-Shafi'i who hold that Zuhr is not nullified at all for excused persons.
4
Apply the conditions
Identify the precise meaning of 'proceeding' (leaving the house), the requirement of hope of catching the prayer, and the exception for excused persons.
The chosen view among Hanafis is that the Balkhi scholars' position (nullification even if one does not hope to catch) is correct, but some conditions remain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن سعى إليها بطل) أي الظهر المؤدى عند أبي حنيفة بمجرد السعي إليها لأنه سمع الجماعة مأمور بعد صلاة الظهر ينقضها بالذهاب إلى الجمعة فالذهاب إليها شروع في طريق نقضها المأمور به فيحكم بنقضها به احتياطاً لترك المعصية. وقالا : لا تبطل حتى يدخل مع الإمام. واختلفوا في معنى السعي إليها والمختار أنه الانفصال عن داره حتى لا يبطل قبله على المختار لأن السعي الرافض لها هو السعي إليها على الخصوص، ومثل ذلك السعي إنما يكون بعد خروجه من باب داره والمراد من السعي المشي لا الإسراع فيه، وإنما عبروا به اتباعاً للآية . وقيد بقوله «سعى لأنه لو كان جالساً في المسجد بعد ما صلى الظهر فإنه لا يبطل حتى يشرع مع الإمام اتفاقاً. كذا في الحقائق. وقيد بقوله «إليها» لأنه لو خرج لحاجة أو خرج وقد فرغ الإمام لم يبطل ظهره إجماعاً، فالبطلان به مقيد بما إذا كان يرجو إدراكها بأن خرج والإمام فيها أو لم يكن شرع وأطلق فشمل ما إذا لم يدركها لبعد المسافة . مع كون الإمام فيها وقت الخروج أو لم يكن شرع وهو قول البلخيين. قال في السراج الوهاج: وهو الصحيح لأنه توجه إليها وهي لم تفت بعد حتى لو كان بيته قريباً من المسجد في الركعة الثانية وتوجه إليها تفت وهي بعد حتى لو كان بيته قريباً من المسجد الجماعة في الركعة الثانية وتوجه بعد ما صلى الظهر في منزله بطل الظهر على الأصح أيضاً لما ذكرنا . وفي النهاية : إذا توجه إليها قبل أن يصليها الإمام ثم إن الإمام لم يصلها لعذر أو لغيره اختلفوا في بطلان ظهره، والصحيح أنها لا تبطل، وكذا لو توجه إليها والإمام والناس فيها إلا أنهم خرجوا منها قبل إتمامها لنائبة فالصحيح أنه لا يبطل ظهره. ثم اعلم أن الضمير المستتر في قوله سعى يعود إلى مصلي الظهر لا إلى من عذر له ليكون أفود وأشمل فإنه لا فرق بين المعذور وغيره في بطلان ظهره بسعيه كما في غاية البيان والسراج الوهاج، لكن التعليل المذكور أولاً لا يشمله لأن المعذور ليس بمأمور بالسعي إليها مطلقاً، فكيف يبطل به؟ فينبغي أن لا يبطل الظهر بالسعي ولا بشروعه في صلاة الجمعة لأن الفرض قد سقط عنه ولم يكن مأموراً بنقضه فتكون الجمعة نفلاً منه كما قاله به زفر والشافعي، وظاهر ما في المحيط أن ظهره إنما يبطل بحضوره الجمعة لا بمجرد سعيه كما في غير المعذور أخف إشكالاً . وسمع البطلان وعبارة السراج هكذا وهذا إذا سعى إليها والإمام في الصلاة أو قبل أن يصلي. وشرط بعض أصحابنا كونه يدركه والصحيح الأول. وفي النهاية : إذا سعى إلى الجمعة قبل أن يصليها الإمام إلا أنه لا يرجو إدراكها لبعد المسافة لم يبطل ظهره في قول العراقيين ويبطل في قول البلخيين وهو الصحيح اهـ. وبها علم عدم صحة ما في النهر من عزوه التقييد للبطلان برجاء إدراكها وتصحيح عدمه حين عدمه إلى السراج وقد تابعه في الدر المختار قوله : (حتى لو كان بيته قريباً من المسجد) أي وبعيداً من باب المسجد كما في السراج قوله : (ثم اعلم أن الضمير المستتر الخ) قال في النهر : الضمير في «صلى» واقع على «من» فما فر منه وقع فيه غاية الأمر أنه سكت عن المعذور قوله : (لكن التعليل أولاً لا يشمله أجاب الشارح: وكذا في الفتح في معرض الجواب عن قول زفر بأنه
His statement: (If he proceeds to it, it becomes void) i.e., the performed Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa nullifies by the mere act of proceeding to it, because he heard that the congregation is commanded after Zuhr prayer to nullify it by going to Jumu'ah, so going to it is a commencement of the commanded way of nullifying it, so it is ruled to be nullified by it as a precaution to avoid sin. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not nullified until he enters with the Imam. They differed on the meaning of 'proceeding to it' and the chosen view is that it means leaving his house, so it is not nullified before that according to the chosen view, because the proceeding that cancels it is specifically the proceeding to it, and such proceeding is only after he exits the door of his house. And what is meant by 'proceeding' is walking, not hurrying. They expressed it this way following the verse. And it is restricted by his saying 'proceeded' because if he was sitting in the mosque after praying Zuhr, it is not nullified until he begins with the Imam by agreement. Thus in al-Haqa'iq. And restricted by his saying 'to it' because if he went out for a need or went out and the Imam had finished, his Zuhr is not nullified by consensus. So its nullification is conditioned upon him hoping to catch it, such that he goes out while the Imam is in it or has not started, and it is general so it includes if he does not catch it due to distance. With the Imam being in it at the time of exit or not having started, and this is the view of the Balkh scholars. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is correct because he headed towards it while it was not yet missed, even if his house is close to the mosque in the second rak'ah and he heads towards it and it is missed, even if his house is close to the mosque... [text has duplication]. In al-Nihayah: If he heads towards it before the Imam prays it, then the Imam does not pray it due to an excuse or otherwise, they differed on the nullification of his Zuhr, and the correct view is that it is not nullified. Similarly, if he heads towards it while the Imam and people are in it, but they left before completing it for some occurrence, the correct view is that his Zuhr is not nullified. Then know that the implicit pronoun in his saying 'proceeded' refers to the one praying Zuhr, not the one with an excuse, to be more beneficial and inclusive, for there is no difference between the excused and others in the nullification of his Zuhr by his proceeding, as in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. But the reasoning mentioned first does not include him because the excused person is not commanded to proceed to it absolutely, so how can it be nullified by it? Therefore, his Zuhr should not be nullified by proceeding nor by his beginning Jumu'ah, because the obligation has fallen from him and he was not commanded to nullify it, so Jumu'ah would be supererogatory for him, as stated by Zufar and al-Shafi'i. And the apparent meaning in al-Muhit is that his Zuhr is only nullified by his attendance at Jumu'ah, not by mere proceeding, as in the non-excused person; it is less problematic. And he heard the nullification, and the statement of al-Siraj is like this: This is if he proceeds to it while the Imam is in prayer or before he prays. And some of our companions condition that he catches it, and the first is correct. In al-Nihayah: If he proceeds to Jumu'ah before the Imam prays it, but he does not hope to catch it due to distance, his Zuhr is not nullified according to the Iraqi scholars, and it is nullified according to the Balkh scholars, and the latter is correct. And by this it is known the incorrectness of what is in al-Nahr attributing the restriction of nullification to hoping to catch it and correcting its absence when absent to al-Siraj, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar followed him. His statement: (Even if his house is close to the mosque) i.e., but far from the door of the mosque, as in al-Siraj. His statement: (Then know that the implicit pronoun etc.) He said in al-Nahr: The pronoun in 'prayed' refers to 'whoever', so what he avoided fell into; the utmost is that he remained silent about the excused. His statement: (But the reasoning first does not include him) The commentator answered: Similarly in al-Fath in the context of answering Zufar's statement that...
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the nullification of the Zuhr prayer when one sets out to attend the Friday congregation. The core ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa is that the Zuhr prayer becomes void by the mere act of proceeding (sai) towards the Jumu'ah congregation, even before joining the Imam. The reasoning is that since the congregation is commanded to nullify their Zuhr and go to Jumu'ah, the act of going is the beginning of that commanded nullification, and to avoid sin, the prayer is considered void. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that the Zuhr is not nullified until actually joining the Imam. The text then defines 'sai' as leaving one's house (not merely moving within the house) and walking at a normal pace, not hurrying. It also specifies conditions: (1) one must be proceeding with the intention to attend Jumu'ah (not for another need); (2) one must have hope of catching the prayer; if it is already too late, the Zuhr is not nullified according to some scholars (the Balkhis say it is nullified regardless, and this is deemed more correct). Additionally, if after proceeding, the Imam does not hold the prayer (due to an excuse) or the congregation disbands, the Zuhr is not nullified. An important nuance: the pronoun in 'proceeded' (saa) refers to the non-excused person, but the excused person (e.g., traveler) is not commanded to proceed, so his Zuhr should not be nullified by proceeding; rather, his Jumu'ah would be supererogatory. This is Zufar's view. The passage concludes with a reference to the correct view among Hanafi scholars (Balkhis vs Iraqis) and corrects a misconception in a later work (al-Nahr).

Key Terms
سعى (sa'ā): In this context, it means to proceed or set out towards the Jumu'ah prayer, specifically by leaving one's house, walking at a normal pace.
بطلان (butlan): Nullification of the prayer; the Zuhr becomes invalid (batil) once one proceeds to Jumu'ah, according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, when does the Zuhr prayer become void for a non-excused person who intends to attend Jumu'ah?
A) Only after he enters the mosque and joins the Imam.
B) As soon as he leaves his house with the intention to go to Jumu'ah.
C) Only after he completes the Zuhr prayer.
D) It never becomes void; he must pray Zuhr again later.

Key Takeaway
The mere act of setting out for Jumu'ah voids the Zuhr in Abu Hanifa's view, provided conditions such as intention and hope of catching are met.

The Invalidation of Zuhr Prayer by Proceeding to Friday: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the conditions and dispute on invalidation of Zuhr by proceeding to Friday.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding when Zuhr becomes invalid upon proceeding to Friday, and apply the Balkhi view to a scenario where the person does not hope to catch the Friday prayer.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, leaving for Friday immediately voids your Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa, but only joining the imam does so according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks a key internal Hanafi disagreement: at what point does a person’s Zuhr prayer become invalid if he sets out to attend Friday prayer? The answer affects how we rule on his Zuhr if he turns back, misses the Friday prayer, or is excused. Understanding the proofs and refinements from the Balkhi and Iraqi scholars will help you navigate this dispute and apply the muftā bihī position in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the legal dispute
The act is ‘sa‘y’ – proceeding to Friday prayer after having already prayed Zuhr. The disputed ruling is whether this act immediately invalidates the Zuhr (Abu Hanifa) or only upon joining the Friday congregation (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad).
Note that ‘sa‘y’ is defined as leaving one’s house, not just intending or walking fast.
2
State the two main positions
Abu Hanifa: invalidation occurs the moment one leaves the house (sa‘y). Sahibayn: invalidation occurs only when one enters the Friday prayer with the imam. Distinguish also between Balkhi (unconditional invalidation on sa‘y) and Iraqi (conditional on hope of catching Friday).
The Balkhi view is adopted as correct by the commentator.
3
Analyze the dalil
The Quranic imperative ‘fas‘aw’ (62:9) is understood as a command to ‘undo’ the Zuhr and focus on Friday. Abu Hanifa reasons that starting the journey is the beginning of that undoing, so precaution demands immediate invalidation. Sahibayn argue the act of walking is not inherently invalidating.
The dalil is zannī al-dalāla, allowing legitimate ikhtilāf.
4
Examine the refinements: Balkhi vs Iraqi
Iraqi scholars condition invalidation on hoping to catch Friday; if the distance is too far, Zuhr remains valid. Balkhi scholars invalidate regardless of hope. The commentator favors the Balkhi view as the correct one.
This distinction affects someone living far from the mosque.
5
Apply to the excused person (ma‘dhūr)
An excused person (e.g., ill, traveller) is not commanded to attend Friday. Therefore, his Zuhr should not be invalidated by proceeding. If he attends, his Friday prayer counts as nafl (Zufar & al-Shāfi‘ī). The reasoning of the excused person is different, so the ruling differs.
The pronoun in ‘sa‘ā’ refers to the non-excused, making the ruling exclusive to them.

Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when does a person's Zuhr prayer become invalid if he proceeds (sa'y) to Friday prayer? The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) states that proceeding invalidates the Zuhr, but the commentator explains the differences. Abu Hanifa holds that the Zuhr is invalidated immediately upon leaving the house (sa'y) because the person is commanded to abandon his Zuhr by attending Friday, so starting the journey is the beginning of that commanded abandonment. Out of precaution against sin, the Zuhr is deemed invalid from that point. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) argue that the Zuhr remains valid until the person actually joins the Friday prayer with the imam, because the act of walking is not inherently invalidating. The commentator also discusses the definition of sa'y: the preferred view is that it means leaving one's house, not just walking quickly, and it is derived from the Quranic verse 'fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' (62:9), where sa'y means walking. The invalidation is further conditioned: if the person was sitting in the mosque after Zuhr, it does not invalidate until he starts with the imam (agreed). If he goes out for a mundane need, or after the imam has finished, the Zuhr remains valid. The passage also addresses the difference between the Iraqi and Balkh scholars: the Iraqis condition invalidation on hope of catching the Friday prayer, while the Balkhis invalidate even if there is no hope due to distance, and this Balkhi view is deemed correct. For an excused person (ma'dhur), the reasoning differs: since he is not commanded to attend Friday, his Zuhr should not be invalidated by proceeding; rather, if he attends, his Friday prayer is nafl. The commentator clarifies that the pronoun in 'sa'a' refers to a non-excused person. The passage ends with a note on intention: if a rustic goes to the city with mixed intentions, the reward depends on the predominant intention, and the follower's Zuhr is not invalidated merely because his imam proceeded.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'ā): The act of proceeding or walking to the Friday prayer; the preferred view is that it means leaving one's house.
بطلان (buṭlān): Invalidation of the earlier Zuhr prayer, meaning it becomes void and must be repeated (or turns into nafl).
معذور (maʿdhūr): A person who has a valid religious or legal excuse from attending Friday prayer, such as illness, travel, or imprisonment.
مأموم (maʾmūm): A follower in prayer; in this context, the one who prays behind an imam in the Zuhr congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It becomes invalid.
C) It becomes nafl automatically.
D) It requires repetition regardless.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the Zuhr becomes invalid immediately upon leaving for Friday, regardless of whether one actually catches the Friday prayer, except for those who are excused.

The Dislike of Congregational Zuhr for the Excused on Friday
Explaining the dislike of congregational Zuhr for excused persons on Friday.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an excused person praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday and explain the reasoning behind the dislike.

Core Idea
Excused person's Zuhr in congregation is valid but disliked to protect Friday attendance.

The Friday prayer is a communal obligation, and the school protects it by discouraging any action that might reduce participation. Even those with a valid excuse from Jumu'ah are advised not to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city, as others may follow their example. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the nuances between the city and countryside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Determine the hukm (legal classification) of the act: praying Zuhr in congregation for an excused person on Friday.
The ruling is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked), not tahrimi.
2
Understand the primary reason (illah)
The main reason given is that others might imitate the excused person and abandon Friday prayer, reducing the congregation.
This is a prevention of harm to the communal obligation.
3
Distinguish city (misr) from countryside (sawad)
The dislike applies only in a city where Friday is established. In the countryside, congregation is not disliked because Friday is not obligatory.
The key is to avoid competing with Friday.
4
Note the validity of the prayer
Despite the dislike, the prayer itself is valid (sahih) because all conditions of Zuhr are met.
Dislike does not affect correctness.
5
Analyze the type of karahah and exceptions
The commentator clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi, not tahrimi. There are exceptions, e.g., if the excused are far from the mosque, congregation may be allowed.
This is an expansion of the base ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكره للمعذور والمسجون أداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر ) لأن المعذور قد يقتدي به غيره فيؤدي إلى تركها، وما علل به في الهداية أولاً بقوله لما فيه من الإخلال بالجمعة إذ هي جامعة للجماعات مبني على عدم جواز تعددها في مصر واحد وهو خلاف المنصوص عليه رواية ودراية . قيد بالمصر لأن الجماعة غير مكروهة في حق أهل السواد لأنه لا جمعة عليهم، وأفاد بالكراهة أن الصلاة صحيحة لاستجماع شرائطها، وفي فتاوي الولوالجي : قوم لا يجب عليهم أن يحضروا الجمعة لبعد الموضع صلوا الظهر جماعة لأنه لا يؤدي إلى تقليل الجماعة في الجمعة ا هـ . فإن كانوا في السواد فظاهر، وإن كانوا في المصر فهي مستثناة من كلام المصنف، ولو حذف المصنف المعذور والمسجون لكان أولى فإن أداء الظهر بجماعة مكروه يوم الجمعة مطلقاً. قال في الظهيرية : جماعة فاتتهم الجمعة في المصر فإنهم يصلون الظهر بغير آذان ولا إقامة ولا جماعة ا هـ . وذكر الولوالجي ولا يصلي يوم الجمعة جماعة في مصر ولا يؤذن ولا يقيم في سجن وغيره لصلاة، ولو زاد أداؤه منفرداً قبل صلاة الإمام لكان أولى لما في الخلاصة : ويستحب للمريض أن يؤخر الصلاة إلى أن يفرغ الإمام من صلاة الجمعة وإن لم يؤخره يكره هو الصحيح ا هـ. ولعله إما لاحتمال أن يقتدي به غيره فيؤدي إلى تركها أو يعافي فيحضرها. وقد اقتصر في المجتبى على الثاني. وإنما صرح بالمسجون مع دخوله في المعذور للاختلاف في أهل السجن فإن السراج الوهاج أن المسجونين إن كانوا ظلمة قدروا على إرضاء الخصوم، وإن كانوا مظلومين أمكنهم الاستغاثة وكان عليهم حضور الجمعة. وقيد بالجماعة لما في التفاريق أن المعذور يصلي الظهر بأذان وإقامة وإن كان لا تستحب الجماعة، وقيد بالظهر لأن في غيرها لا بأس أن يصلوا جماعة. وأشار المصنف إلى أن المساجد تغلق . الجمعة إلا الجامع يوم لثلا يجتمع إنما رخص له تركها للعذر وبالإلتزام التحق بالصحيح قوله : ولو) حذف المصنف وقوله الآتي ولو زاد أو أداؤه الخ) قال في النهر : أما الحذف كما ذكر فغير محتاج إليه لأنه معلوم بالأولى، وأما الزيادة فلأنها توهم . أن الكراهة فيها كالتي قبلها تحريمية وظاهر الخلاصة يقتضي أنها تنزيهية قوله : (في سجن وغيره لصلاة عبارة الولوالجية لصلاة الظهر.
His statement: (And it is disliked for the excused and the imprisoned to perform Zuhr in congregation in the city) because the excused might be followed by others, leading to abandonment of Friday. The reasoning given first in al-Hidayah, 'because it involves violation of the Friday prayer since it is the gathering of congregations', is based on the impermissibility of multiple Friday prayers in one city, which contradicts the transmitted and reasoned texts. He restricted to the city because congregation is not disliked for villagers since Friday is not obligatory on them. The dislike indicates that the prayer is valid as it meets all conditions. In Fatawa al-Walwaliji: People on whom Friday is not obligatory due to distance, if they pray Zuhr in congregation, it does not lead to reducing the congregation in Friday. So if they are in the countryside, it is clear; if they are in the city, it is excepted from the author's statement. It would have been better if the author had omitted the excused and imprisoned, because praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked absolutely. Al-Zahiriyyah said: A congregation that missed Friday in the city pray Zuhr without adhan, iqamah, or congregation. Al-Walwaliji mentioned: One should not pray in congregation on Friday in a city, nor give adhan or iqamah in prison or elsewhere for prayer. It is better if he prays alone before the imam's prayer, because in al-Khulasa: It is recommended for the sick to delay prayer until the imam finishes Friday; if he does not delay, it is disliked; this is the correct view. Perhaps it is because others might follow him leading to abandonment, or he might recover and attend. Al-Mujtaba restricted to the second reason. He explicitly mentioned the imprisoned along with the excused because of the difference regarding prisoners: al-Siraj al-Wahhaj states that if they are oppressors, they can satisfy the claimants; if they are oppressed, they can seek help, and Friday is obligatory on them. He restricted to congregation because in al-Tafariq: The excused prays Zuhr with adhan and iqamah even though congregation is not recommended. He restricted to Zuhr because for other prayers there is no problem to pray in congregation. The author indicated that mosques are locked on Friday except the congregational mosque so that they do not gather. He was only permitted to leave it due to excuse, and by undertaking it he becomes like a sound person. His statement: (And if) the author omitted, and his upcoming statement 'and if he added or performed it etc.' Al-Nahr said: As for the omission as mentioned, it is unnecessary because it is known by priority. As for the addition, it gives the impression that the dislike is like the previous one (tahrimi), but the apparent meaning of al-Khulasa is that it is tanzihi. His statement: (in prison and elsewhere for prayer) the phrase of al-Walwalijiyyah is: 'for Zuhr prayer'.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of karahah (dislike) for a person who has a valid excuse from Friday prayer (such as illness, travel, or imprisonment) to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city (misr). The primary reason given is that if an excused person prays in congregation, others might follow him, leading to the abandonment of the Friday prayer. The commentator critiques the reasoning from al-Hidayah that it causes 'violation of the Friday prayer because Friday is the gathering of congregations,' noting that this reasoning assumes multiple Friday prayers are not allowed in one city, which is not the consensus. The dislike is specific to the city because villagers, upon whom Friday is not obligatory, may pray in congregation without dislike. The prayer itself remains valid (sahih) as all conditions are met. The passage also cites various authorities: Fatawa al-Walwaliji allows congregation for those far from the mosque, but only in the countryside. Al-Zahiriyyah states that those who miss Friday in the city should pray Zuhr alone, without adhan, iqamah, or congregation. Al-Walwaliji also forbids congregation in the city on Friday. The commentator notes that it would have been better if the author (Kanz al-Daqaiq) omitted the mention of the excused and imprisoned, because praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked absolutely for everyone, even those without excuse. The reason for specifying the imprisoned is because of the disagreement: according to al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, prisoners may actually be obligated to attend Friday if they are oppressors (who can make amends) or oppressed (who can seek help). The restriction to congregation means that an excused person may pray Zuhr with adhan and iqamah individually, though congregation is not recommended. Finally, the commentator discusses whether the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) or tanzihi (lightly disliked), concluding that it is tanzihi based on al-Khulasa.

Key Terms
معذور (maʿdhūr): One who has a valid legal excuse from performing the Friday prayer, such as illness, travel, or imprisonment.
مسجون (masjūn): An imprisoned person; there is difference as to whether Friday is obligatory on them.
كراهة (karāha): Dislike; in this context, it is tanzihi (close to permissible) not tahrimi (close to forbidden).
مصر (miṣr): A major city or town where Friday prayer is established; opposite of 'sawad' (countryside).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the dislike for an excused person's congregational Zuhr on Friday restricted to the city (misr)?
A) Because the city has larger population and the risk of reducing Friday attendance is greater.
B) Because Friday prayer is not obligatory in the countryside.
C) Because the excused person is not allowed to pray in the city.
D) Because the mosque in the city is closed on Friday.

Key Takeaway
The excused person's Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday is valid but makruh tanzih; individual prayer is recommended.

Catching Jumu'ah in Tashahhud or Sajdat al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on catching Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer who catches the tashahhud of Jumu'ah and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A latecomer who catches even the tashahhud of Jumu'ah has caught the prayer according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

This lesson examines a practical scenario: you arrive late to Friday prayer and find the imam in the final sitting or even in the prostration of forgetfulness. Have you caught the Jumu'ah prayer, or must you pray Zuhr? The Hanafi school has a well-known difference between its founding imams on this very point. Understanding the reasoning helps you appreciate how the school handles partial participation in collective worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The latecomer joins the imam in the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw of Jumu'ah.
This is not catching a full rak'ah; it is catching only the final sitting or the forgetfulness prostration.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
The latecomer has caught Jumu'ah and completes two rak'ahs.
They consider the conditions of Jumu'ah to be fulfilled through the imam, so the latecomer builds on the imam's prayer.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
If he caught more than half of the second rak'ah, he builds on it as Jumu'ah; if less, he builds on it as Zuhr and prays four rak'ahs.
Muhammad distinguishes based on the amount of the second rak'ah caught.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The two positions (Jumu'ah and Zuhr) are contradictory and cannot be combined in a single prayer. Hence the latecomer is fully considered to have caught Jumu'ah.
The imam's conditions are attributed to the latecomer.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is the position stated in the matn and supported by the majority of later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سجود السهو أثم جمعة وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام ويجب السعي إليها وترك فيها جماعة . كذا في السراج الوهاج وظاهر كلامهم أن الكراهة في مسألة الكتاب تحريمية لأن الجماعة مؤدية إلى الحرام وما أدى إليه فهو مكروه تحريماً قوله : (ومن أدركها في التشهد : معه أو في سجود السهو أتم جمعة) يعني عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف . وقال محمد: إن أدرك . أكثر الركعة الثانية بني عليها الجمعة وإن أدرك أقلها بنى عليها الظهر لأنه جمعة من وجه ظهر من وجه لفوات بعض الشرائط في حقه فيصلي أربعاً اعتباراً للظهر، ويقعد لا محالة على رأس الركعتين اعتباراً للجمعة ويقرأ في الأخريين لاحتمال النفلية. ولهما: إنه مدرك للجمعة في هذه الحالة حتى تشترط نية الجمعة وهي ركعتان ولا وجه لما ذكر لأنهما مختلفان لا ينبني أحدهما على تحريمة الآخر، ووجود الشرائط في حق الإمام يجعل موجوداً في حق المسبوق. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله إلى أنه لا بد أن ينوي الجمعة دون الظهر حتى لو نوى الظهر لم يصح اقتداؤه. كذا في المبسوط وفي المضمرات إنه مجمع عليه. وأشار أيضاً إلى أن الإمام يسجد للسهو في الجمعة والعيدين والمختار عند المتأخرين أن لا يسجد في الجمعة والعيدين لتوهم الزيادة من الجهال كذا في السراج الوهاج وغيره. ثم إذا قام هذا المسبوق إلى قضائه كان مخيراً في القراءة إن شاء جهر وإن شاء خافت كذا في السراج الوهاج أيضاً. وفي المجتبى : ولو زحمه الناس فلم يستطع السجود فوقف حتى سلم الإمام فهو لاحق يمضي في صلاته بغير قراءة ا.هـ. وقيد بالجمعة لأن من أدرك الإمام في صلاة العيد في التشهد فإنه يتم العيد اتفاقاً. كذا في فتح القدير من صلاة العيد. وذكر في السراج أن عند محمد لم يصر مدركاً للعيد. وفي الظهيرية معزياً إلى المنتقى : مسافر أدرك الإمام يوم الجمعة في التشهد يصلي أربعاً بالتكبير الذي دخل فيه ا هـ . وهو مخصص لما في المتون مقتض لحملها على ما إذا كانت الجمعة واجبة على المسبوق أما إذا لم تكن واجبة فإنه يتم ظهراً.
Sajdat al-sahw is [؟] Jumu'ah. And when the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech, and it is obligatory to walk to it and to leave congregation in it. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the apparent meaning of their words is that the dislike in the issue of the book is tahrimi, because the congregation leads to haram and what leads to it is makruh tahrimi. His statement: (And whoever catches it in the tashahhud: with him or in sajdat al-sahw, he completes Jumu'ah) meaning according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: If he catches most of the second rak'ah, he builds on it as Jumu'ah; if he catches less, he builds on it as Zuhr, because it is Jumu'ah in one aspect and Zuhr in another due to the loss of some conditions in his right. So he prays four, considering Zuhr, and he sits inevitably at the end of two rak'ahs considering Jumu'ah, and he recites in the last two because of the possibility of nafl. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): he is one who caught Jumu'ah in this situation, so the intention of Jumu'ah is required and it is two rak'ahs. There is no basis for what he mentioned because the two are different, one cannot be built upon the other's tahrima, and the presence of conditions in the right of the imam makes them present in the right of the latecomer. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that he must intend Jumu'ah, not Zuhr; if he intended Zuhr, his following is not valid. Thus in al-Mabsut and in al-Mudamarat it is agreed upon. He also indicated that the imam performs sajdat al-sahw in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids. The chosen view according to the later scholars is that he should not perform sajdat al-sahw in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids to avoid the assumption of increase by the ignorant, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others. Then when this latecomer stands to complete his prayer, he has a choice in recitation: if he wishes he recites aloud, if he wishes he recites silently, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj also. And in al-Mujtaba: if people crowded him and he could not prostrate, so he stood until the imam said salam, he is a lahiq and continues his prayer without recitation. End. He restricted it to Jumu'ah because one who catches the imam in 'Eid prayer in tashahhud completes 'Eid by agreement, as in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter of 'Eid prayer. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj that according to Muhammad he is not considered to have caught 'Eid. In al-Zahiriyya, attributed to al-Muntaqa: a traveler who caught the imam on Friday in tashahhud prays four with the takbir with which he entered. End. And it is a specification of what is in the texts, implying that they are carried on the case where Jumu'ah is obligatory on the latecomer; if it is not obligatory, then he completes Zuhr.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a person who joins the imam during the final tashahhud or the prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) in Friday prayer. According to the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), such a person has caught the Jumu'ah prayer and completes it as two rak'ahs. Imam Muhammad, however, distinguishes between catching more or less than half of the second rak'ah. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage also discusses that the imam should not perform sajdat al-sahw in Jumu'ah or 'Eid prayers to avoid confusion for the ignorant. After the imam completes, the latecomer may choose whether to recite aloud or silently. Additionally, if the latecomer is a traveler for whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory, he prays four rak'ahs (Zuhr) instead.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the congregation after the imam has already started; a latecomer.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting of the final part of the prayer reciting the tashahhud.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He prays two rak'ahs as Jumu'ah.
B) He prays four rak'ahs as Zuhr.
C) He repeats the prayer.
D) He joins the imam and then leaves.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that a latecomer who catches the imam in the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw of Jumu'ah has caught the Friday prayer and prays two rak'ahs.

Prohibition of Prayer and Speech When the Imam Emerges for Friday Khutbah
Ruling with proof on Friday prayer and speech prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on initiating prayer and speech after the imam's emergence on Friday, and identify the proof from the companions' practice.

Core Idea
Once the imam appears for the khutbah, no new prayer or speech is allowed—even answering the adhan.

This lesson examines a key rule of Friday congregation: the moment the imam emerges from his place to ascend the minbar, all supererogatory prayers and speech become prohibited. The ruling is derived from the practice of the Companions and has implications for the adhan and other activities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is initiating any prayer or speaking after the imam emerges. The ruling is prohibition: starting a new prayer is invalid and sinful, while speech is makruh tahrimi.
The text uses 'no prayer and no speech' which indicates a strong prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a narration from Ibn Abi Shayba that three Companions (Ali, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar) disliked prayer and speech after the imam's emergence. In Hanafi usul, qawl al-sahabi is considered hujjah (proof).
The term 'yakrahoon' (they disliked) indicates disapproval, and in this context, it implies prohibition.
3
Interpret 'emergence' and scope
The commentator explains that 'emergence' means the imam ascending the minbar or appearing from his compartment (maqsurah). The prohibition includes answering the adhan, but recitation and dhikr are allowed if the imam has not yet appeared.
If the mosque has no maqsurah, the people may continue reciting until the imam stands up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا (كلام لما رواه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه عن علي وابن عباس وابن عمر رضي الله عنهم كانوا يكرهون الصلاة والكلام بعد خروج الإمام . وقول الصحابي حجة ولأن الكلام يمتد طبعاً فيخل بالاستماع والصلاة قد تستلزمه أيضاً. و به اندفع قولهما إنه لا بأس بالكلام إذا خرج قبل أن يخطب وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر. وأجمعوا أن الخروج قاطع للصلاة. وفي العيون المراد إجابة المؤذن، أما غيره من الكلام فيكره إجماعاً. كذا في السراج الوهاج وفسر الشارح الخروج بالصعود على المنبر وهكذا في المضمرات. وذكر في السراج الوهاج يعني خرج من المقصورة وظهر عليهم، وقيل صعد المنبر فإن لم يكن في المستجد مقصورة يخرج منها لم يتركوا القراءة والذكر لا إذا قام الإمام إلى قوله: (وهو مخصص لما في المتون الخ) قال في النهر : الظاهر أن هذا مخرج على قول محمد،
His statement: (And when the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech) because of what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf from 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them: they disliked prayer and speech after the imam's emergence. And the statement of a companion is a proof. And because speech naturally extends and disturbs listening, and prayer may also necessitate it. And by this their statement that there is no harm in speech if he comes out before he delivers the khutbah and if he descends before he says takbir is refuted. And they agreed that emergence cuts off prayer. In al-'Uyun: what is intended is answering the mu'adhdhin; as for other speech, it is disliked by consensus. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the commentator interpreted 'emergence' as ascending the minbar, and likewise in al-Mudamarat. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: meaning he came out of the compartment and appeared to them; and it is said he ascended the minbar. If the mosque has no compartment from which to emerge, they do not leave recitation and dhikr, except when the imam stands up to his statement: (And it is a specification of what is in the texts etc.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently this is based on the saying of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage comments on the prohibition of prayer and speech after the imam emerges for the Friday khutbah. The proof is a hadith from the companions, whose statements are considered hujjah. The prohibition applies to initiating any new prayer and to speaking (including answering the adhan). The reason is that speech distracts from listening to the khutbah, and prayer also involves movement. The phrase 'emergence' is interpreted as the imam ascending the minbar or appearing from the compartment (maqsurah). If the imam has not yet ascended, recitation and dhikr are allowed. The relied-upon view is that this prohibition is makruh tahrimi for speech and more severe for prayer.

Key Terms
الخروج (al-khuruj): The emergence of the imam from his place to ascend the minbar for the khutbah.
قاطع للصلاة (qati' li al-salah): Something that cuts off or invalidates the prayer; once the imam emerges, no new prayer should be started.
قول الصحابي (qawl al-sahabi): A statement or ruling of a companion of the Prophet, considered a source of evidence in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The emergence of the imam on Friday cuts off all supererogatory prayers and speech to ensure focus on the khutbah.

Ruling on Imam's Sajda al-Sahw in Jumu'ah
States that the imam's sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah is makruh tahrimi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam performing sajda al-sahw during Jumu'ah and explain why it is considered makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
The imam's sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah is makruh tahrimi because it creates confusion akin to adding to the prayer.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the imam's prostration of forgetfulness during Jumu'ah prayer. While sajda al-sahw is generally wajib in many cases, the context of Jumu'ah changes its ruling. We will explore why the Hanafi school considers it prohibitively disliked and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is the imam performing sajda al-sahw during Jumu'ah prayer. The text states that this is a sin (ithm), which the commentator interprets as makruh tahrimi.
The base matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq; the commentator is Ibn Nujaym.
2
Understand the type of karahah
The commentator specifies that the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), not tanzihi. This is a higher level of dislike, close to haram.
In Hanafi fiqh, makruh tahrimi is based on speculative evidence and carries a stronger prohibition than makruh tanzihi.
3
Grasp the reasoning
The reasoning given is that performing sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah may lead to something forbidden (haram). The phrase 'al-jama'ah mu'addiyat ila al-haram' indicates that the congregation's perception could lead to confusion or innovation.
The principle 'ma adda ila al-haram fa-huwa makruh tahriman' is a key maxim in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سجود السهو أثم جمعة . كذا في السراج الوهاج وظاهر كلامهم أن الكراهة في مسألة الكتاب تحريمية لأن الجماعة مؤدية إلى الحرام وما أدى إليه فهو مكروه تحريماً
Sajda al-sahw is a sin in Jumu'ah. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and apparent from their speech is that the prohibition in the matter of the book is prohibitively disliked, because congregation leads to the forbidden, and whatever leads to it is prohibitively disliked.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the imam's performance of sajda al-sahw during Jumu'ah prayer. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah is a sin. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains that according to al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and the apparent meaning of the scholars' words, the karahah in this matter is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The reasoning is that the congregation itself may lead to something forbidden, and whatever leads to the forbidden is itself makruh tahrimi. Thus, the imam should avoid performing sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
كراهة تحريمية (karaha tahrimiyya): A disliked action that is close to haram, based on a speculative proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the imam performing sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah prayer according to the relied-upon position?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The imam should not perform sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah; it is prohibitively disliked because it can lead to confusion among the congregation.

Masbuq Catching Imam in Tashahhud or Sajda al-Sahw of Jumu'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq completing Jumu'ah when catching only tashahhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the masbuq's obligation in Jumu'ah when catching the imam in the final tashahhud or sajda al-sahw, and evaluate the differing view of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
A latecomer who catches the imam in the final tashahhud of Jumu'ah completes Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs, not Zuhr—according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the ruling for a latecomer (masbuq) who joins the Jumu'ah prayer when the imam is already in the final tashahhud or performing sajda al-sahw? While the base text states that he completes Jumu'ah, a minority position within the school (Imam Muhammad) argues otherwise. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi methodology for reconciling conditions of Jumu'ah and the nature of following the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Masbuq's Situation
The latecomer catches the imam only in the final tashahhud or sajda al-sahw of Jumu'ah. He has missed most of the second rak'ah.
The masbuq joins during the final sitting or prostration of forgetfulness.
2
State the Hanafi Position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
The masbuq completes Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs. He must intend Jumu'ah, not Zuhr. After the imam's salam, he stands to complete his missed rak'ah.
This is the zahir al-riwayah and mufta bihi position.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's Counterposition
Muhammad argues that if the masbuq catches less than half of the second rak'ah (i.e., only the tashahhud), he must pray Zuhr (four rak'ahs) because he missed the conditions of Jumu'ah. However, he sits after two rak'ahs to respect the possibility of Jumu'ah.
Muhammad considers the loss of attending the khutbah and the rak'ah as breaking the Jumu'ah connection.
4
Understand the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
The two imams respond that conditions fulfilled by the imam are considered present for the masbuq. The masbuq's construction is separate from the imam's, so he builds his own rak'ah upon the imam's tahrima. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as indicated in al-Mabsut.
The tarjih authority: 'the author indicated' and 'it is agreed upon' in al-Mabsut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن أدركها في التشهد معه أو في سجود السهو أتم جمعة) يعني عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف . وقال محمد: إن أدرك أكثر الركعة الثانية بني عليها الجمعة وإن أدرك أقلها بنى عليها الظهر لأنه جمعة من وجه ظهر من وجه لفوات بعض الشرائط في حقه فيصلي أربعاً اعتباراً للظهر، ويقعد لا محالة على رأس الركعتين اعتباراً للجمعة ويقرأ في الأخريين لاحتمال النفلية. ولهما: إنه مدرك للجمعة في هذه الحالة حتى تشترط نية الجمعة وهي ركعتان ولا وجه لما ذكر لأنهما مختلفان لا ينبني أحدهما على تحريمة الآخر، ووجود الشرائط في حق الإمام يجعل موجوداً في حق المسبوق. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله إلى أنه لا بد أن ينوي الجمعة دون الظهر حتى لو نوى الظهر لم يصح اقتداؤه. كذا في المبسوط وفي المضمرات إنه مجمع عليه. وأشار أيضاً إلى أن الإمام يسجد للسهو في الجمعة والعيدين والمختار عند المتأخرين أن لا يسجد في الجمعة والعيدين لتوهم الزيادة من الجهال كذا في السراج الوهاج وغيره. ثم إذا قام هذا المسبوق إلى قضائه كان مخيراً في القراءة إن شاء جهر وإن شاء خافت كذا في السراج الوهاج أيضاً. وفي المجتبى : ولو زحمه الناس فلم يستطع السجود فوقف حتى سلم الإمام فهو لاحق يمضي في صلاته بغير قراءة ا.هـ. وقيد بالجمعة لأن من أدرك الإمام في صلاة العيد في التشهد فإنه يتم العيد اتفاقاً. كذا في فتح القدير من صلاة العيد. وذكر في السراج أن عند محمد لم يصر مدركاً للعيد. وفي الظهيرية معزياً إلى المنتقى : مسافر أدرك الإمام يوم الجمعة في التشهد يصلي أربعاً بالتكبير الذي دخل فيه ا هـ . وهو مخصص لما في المتون مقتض لحملها على ما إذا كانت الجمعة واجبة على المسبوق أما إذا لم تكن واجبة فإنه يتم ظهراً.
His statement: (And whoever catches it in the tashahhud with him or in sajda al-sahw completes Jumu'ah) means according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: If he catches more than half of the second rak'ah, he builds Jumu'ah upon it; if he catches less, he builds Zuhr upon it because it is Jumu'ah from one aspect and Zuhr from another due to the loss of some conditions in his right. So he prays four rak'ahs considering Zuhr, and he sits inevitably at the end of two rak'ahs considering Jumu'ah, and recites in the last two due to the possibility of supererogatory. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) have that he is a catch-er of Jumu'ah in this situation, so that the intention of Jumu'ah is required, and it is two rak'ahs, and there is no basis for what was mentioned because they are different, one cannot be built upon the tahrima of the other, and the existence of conditions in the right of the imam makes it exist in the right of the masbuq. And the author indicated that he must intend Jumu'ah not Zuhr, such that if he intended Zuhr his following would not be valid. Thus in al-Mabsut and in al-Mudmarat it is agreed upon. And he also indicated that the imam performs sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids, and the chosen according to the later scholars is that he does not perform sajda in Jumu'ah and 'Eid due to the suspicion of increase from the ignorant, thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others. Then when this masbuq stands to complete his prayer, he has a choice in recitation: if he wishes he may recite aloud or silently, thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj as well. And in al-Mujtaba: And if the people crowded him so he could not prostrate, so he stood until the imam said salam, then he is a lahiq, he continues his prayer without recitation. And it is restricted to Jumu'ah because whoever catches the imam in 'Eid prayer in tashahhud, he completes 'Eid by agreement. Thus in Fath al-Qadir from the book of 'Eid prayer. And mentioned in al-Siraj that according to Muhammad he does not become a catch-er of 'Eid. And in al-Zahiriya referencing al-Muntaqa: A traveller caught the imam on Friday in tashahhud, he prays four rak'ahs with the takbir with which he entered. This specifies the general texts, necessitating that they be interpreted as when Jumu'ah is obligatory on the masbuq; if not obligatory, he completes Zuhr.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a latecomer (masbuq) who joins the Jumu'ah prayer when the imam is in the final tashahhud or in sajda al-sahw. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that such a person completes Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs. The commentator explains that this is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs: if the masbuq catches more than half of the second rak'ah (i.e., the rukn of the second rak'ah like ruku'), he builds Jumu'ah upon it; if he catches less (e.g., only the tashahhud), he builds Zuhr upon it, because in his case some conditions of Jumu'ah are missing, so he prays four rak'ahs as Zuhr, but he must sit after two rak'ahs to respect Jumu'ah. The reasoning of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the masbuq is considered a catch-er of Jumu'ah in this situation, so he must intend Jumu'ah and it remains two rak'ahs. They argue that the imam's rak'ahs are not built upon the masbuq's because they are different constructions, and the imam's fulfillment of conditions makes those conditions present for the masbuq. The author also mentions that the imam's sajda al-sahw in Jumu'ah is makruh according to later scholars. Then the passage gives additional rulings: the masbuq may recite aloud or silently when completing his prayer; if he cannot prostrate due to crowding, he becomes a lahiq and continues without recitation; and the discussion about a traveler (musafir) catching the imam in tashahhud. The overall principle is that the masbuq completes Jumu'ah if it was obligatory on him; otherwise, he completes Zuhr.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has started, but catches only part of the prayer.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who is prevented from following the imam due to a valid excuse (e.g., crowding) and continues independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a person catches the imam in the final tashahhud of Jumu'ah, what should he do?
A) He should complete Jumu'ah as four rak'ahs.
B) He should complete Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs.
C) He should pray Zuhr instead.
D) He should leave the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The stronger Hanafi view is that a masbuq who catches the imam in tashahhud completes Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs, because the imam's fulfillment of conditions suffices for the masbuq.

Prohibition of Prayer and Speech After Imam's Exit for Jumu'ah
Ruling with proof on prohibition of prayer and speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer and speech after the imam exits for Jumu'ah, identify the proof from the Companions' practice, and apply the correct interpretation of the hadiths concerning the khutbah.

Core Idea
No prayer and no speech after the imam exits for Jumu'ah — the exit cuts all voluntary acts.

This lesson examines the well-known Hanafi ruling that upon the imam's emergence for the Jumu'ah khutbah, all prayer and speech become prohibited. We will trace the proofs from the Companions' practice, the rational basis, and address apparent contradictions with authentic hadiths. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the sanctity and focus of the Friday sermon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech.' Determine the hukm level for each: prayer is haram (to initiate), speech is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The prohibition applies to all prayers, including sunnah and tahiyyat al-masjid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of the Companions (Ali, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar) narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba that they disliked prayer and speech after the imam's exit. Also rational reasoning: speech disrupts listening; prayer may also cause disruption.
Qawl al-sahabi is a hujja in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'يكرهون' indicates disapproval, but the context of the prohibition and the rational argument elevate it to tahrim. The hadith 'If you say to your companion... you have engaged in idle talk' implies a fortiori that prayer, which is more distracting, is also prohibited.
The hadith about praying two rak'ahs upon entering (Sahih Muslim) is interpreted as abrogated or applicable before the prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed speech after the imam's exit but before he starts the khutbah, and also when he descends before the takbir. The text refutes this by consensus and by the Companion practice.
The term 'قولهما' refers to the two disciples of Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is that prayer (including sunnah and tahiyyat) is prohibited at the moment of exit; speech is prohibited except for answering the adhan or commanding good. The hadith in Sahih Muslim is interpreted as applying before the ruling of prohibition was established, or as a special case for the latecomer who must pray two rak'ahs before sitting, but this is not the preferred view in the Hanafi school.
The text also discusses that the definition of 'exit' varies: if the imam has an enclosure, exit means coming out; otherwise, standing to ascend the minbar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام) لما رواه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه عن علي وابن عباس وابن عمر رضي الله عنهم كانوا يكرهون الصلاة والكلام بعد خروج الإمام . وقول الصحابي حجة ولأن الكلام يمتد طبعاً فيخل بالاستماع والصلاة قد تستلزمه أيضاً. و به اندفع قولهما إنه لا بأس بالكلام إذا خرج قبل أن يخطب وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر. وأجمعوا أن الخروج قاطع للصلاة. وفي العيون المراد إجابة المؤذن، أما غيره من مثال لا قيد ا هـ. ويؤيده ما مر في الرد على محمد قوله : (وهو أعلى من السنة وتحية المسجد كان المناسب إسقاط قوله «وهو» ليكون قوله «أعلى» خبر «أن» . کتاب (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الجمعة باب ٣٦ مسلم في الصلاة باب ۲۳۱ الدارمي في " الصلاة باب ١٩٦ . أحمد في مسنده (٣/ ٢٩٧) (٢٠٣/٦).
His statement: (And when the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech) because of what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf from 'Ali, Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that they disliked prayer and speech after the imam's exit. And the saying of a Companion is a proof, and because speech naturally extends and disrupts listening, and prayer may also entail it. And with this is refuted their statement that there is no harm in speech if he comes out before delivering the khutbah and when he descends before saying takbir. And they are agreed that the exit is a cutter for prayer. And in al-'Uyun, what is intended is answering the mu'adhdhin; as for other speech, it is disliked by consensus. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and the commentator interpreted exit as ascending the minbar, and similarly in al-Mudmarat. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that it means he came out of the enclosure and appeared to them, and it was said he ascended the minbar. If there is no enclosure in the mosque to come out of, they do not leave off recitation and dhikr, no, when the imam stands for the khutbah. And in Sharh al-Majma': The expression of exit is used according to the custom of the Arabs that they used to take an empty place for veneration, so he would exit from it when he intended to ascend. Thus we saw it in their lands, and the cutter in our lands is the imam's standing to ascend. So the conclusion is that if the imam is in seclusion, the cutter is his separation from it and his appearance to the people; otherwise, his standing to ascend. And he made 'prayer' absolute, so it includes sunnah and tahiyyat al-masjid, and the hadith indicates it: 'If you say to your companion while the imam is delivering the khutbah on Friday: Listen, you have engaged in idle talk.' This indicates by implication their prohibition a fortiori, because forbidding good is higher than sunnah and tahiyyat al-masjid. And what is in Sahih Muslim from his saying: 'If one of you comes while the imam is delivering the khutbah, let him pray two rak'ahs and make them light.' This is interpreted as before the prohibition of speech, to avoid contradiction. And their response by interpreting it as when he pauses from the khutbah until he finishes his prayer, as they answered in the incident of Sulayk al-Ghatafani, is not suitable for the madhhab of the Imam because you know that prayer is prevented merely by his exit before the khutbah until he finishes the prayer. And in Fath al-Qadir: And if he comes out while he is in the sunnah, he cuts off at two rak'ahs. This is a weak statement, and Qadikhan attributed it to al-Nawadir. He said: If he cuts off, four rak'ahs become necessary for him. The correct is the opposite, as in al-Muhit. Al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa: If he began the four before Jumu'ah then the khutbah started, or the four before Zuhr then the iqama was called, should he cut off at the end of two rak'ahs? They discussed it, and the correct is that he completes and does not cut because it is like a single obligatory prayer. And similarly in al-Mubtaghi, and it does not affect the making up of a missed prayer that did not drop the order between it and the time-based prayer, for it is not disliked as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj because he made absolute what he previously mentioned that order is obligatory in the sense of condition. And he made absolute in the prohibition of speech, so it includes the khatib. He said in al-Bada'i: It is disliked for the khatib to speak during the khutbah, except if it is commanding good, then it is not disliked, because it is narrated that the Prophet was delivering the khutbah on Friday and 'Uthman entered, so he said to him: What time is this? He said: I did nothing more when I heard the call, O Commander of the Faithful, except that I performed wudu. So he said: ... and the traveler is an example, not a restriction. And supported by what passed in the refutation of Muhammad: 'It is higher than sunnah and tahiyyat al-masjid.' The appropriate would be to drop the word 'huwa' so that 'a'la' is the predicate of 'anna'.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prohibition of prayer and speech after the imam comes out for the Jumu'ah khutbah. The matn states: 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech.' The commentator provides several proofs: a narration from Ibn Abi Shayba that the Companions disliked prayer and speech after the imam's exit, which is a proof (qawl al-sahabi). Also rational reasoning: speech disrupts listening to the khutbah, and prayer may also cause disruption. The text then refutes the view of some that speech is allowed before the khutbah. Then it discusses the definition of 'exit': whether it means ascending the minbar, coming out of the enclosure, or standing up. The preferred interpretation according to the commentator is that if the imam is in a separate room, exit means coming out; otherwise, it's standing to ascend. The prohibition includes all prayers, even sunnah and tahiyyat al-masjid, and the hadith 'if you say to your companion...' supports this a fortiori. The hadith from Sahih Muslim about praying two rak'ahs when arriving during the khutbah is interpreted as applying before the prohibition was established. The text also addresses the issue of cutting a supererogatory prayer when the imam comes out: the correct view is that one does not cut it but completes it, because it is like a single obligatory prayer. Finally, it discusses the khatib speaking during the khutbah: it is disliked unless it is commanding good.

Key Terms
خروج الإمام (khuruj al-imam): The imam's emergence from his place to ascend the minbar for the Jumu'ah khutbah. In the Hanafi school, it is the trigger for the prohibition of prayer and speech.
كلام (kalam): Speech, including conversation, answering, etc., during the khutbah.
قاطع (qati'): The 'cutter' – the imam's exit is a qati' for prayer, meaning it prohibits starting new prayers and, according to some, may cut an ongoing prayer (though the correct view is that one completes an ongoing prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm of a person who starts praying two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid after the imam has already ascended the minbar for the Jumu'ah khutbah?
A) The prayer is valid and recommended.
B) The prayer is makruh but valid.
C) The prayer is haram (prohibited to initiate).
D) The prayer is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Upon the imam's exit for the Jumu'ah khutbah, it is prohibited to initiate any prayer (including sunnah and tahiyyat) and to speak (except for essential matters like commanding good or answering the adhan).
