قوله (وندب يوم الفطر أن يطعم ويغتسل ويستاك ويتطيب ويلبس أحسن ثيابه) اقتداء بالنبي . ويستحب كون ذلك المطعوم حلواً لما روى البخاري : كان عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يغدو يوم الفطر حتى يأكل تمرات ويأكلهن وتراً . وأما ما يفعله الناس في زماننا من جمع التمر مع اللبن والفطر عليه فليس له أصل في السنة، وظاهر كلامهم تقديم الأحسن من الثياب في الجمعة والعيدين وإن لم يكن أبيض والدليل دال عليه فقد روى البيهقي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يلبس يوم العيد بردة حمراء. وفي فتح القدير: واعلم أن الحلة الحمراء عبارة عن ثوبين من اليمن فيهما خطوط حمر وخضر لا أنها أحمر بحت فليكن محمل البردة أحدهما اهـ. بدليل نهيه عليه السلام عن لبس الأحمر كما رواه أبو داود والقول مقدم على الفعل والحاظر مقدم على المبيح لو تعارضا فكيف إذا لم يتعارضا بالحمل المذكور. وزاد في الحاوي القدسي أن من المستحبات التزين وأن يظهر فرحاً وبشاشة ويكثر من الصدقة حسب طاقته وقدرته. وزاد في القنية استحباب التختم والتبكير وهو سرعة الانتباه والابتكار وهو المسارعة إلى المصلى وصلاة الغداة في مسجد حيه والخروج إلى المصلى ماشياً والرجوع في طريق آخر والتهنئة بقوله «تقبل الله منا ومنكم لا تنكر . وفي المجتبى : فإن قلت عد الغسل ههنا مستحباً وفي الطهارة سنة قلت : للاختلاف فيه والصحيح أنه سنة، وسماه مستحباً لاشتمال السنة على المستحب وعد سائر المستحبات المذكورة هنا في بعض الكتب سنة .اهـ.
His statement: 'And it is recommended on the day of Fitr that he eat, perform ghusl, use the miswak, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes' following the example of the Prophet. And it is desirable that the food be sweet, because Bukhari narrated: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he ate some dates, and he would eat them odd in number.' As for what people in our time do of mixing dates with milk and breaking the fast on that, it has no basis in the Sunnah. The apparent meaning of their words is to give precedence to the best of clothes in Jumuah and the two Eids, even if it is not white; the evidence indicates it, as al-Bayhaqi narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to wear on the day of Eid a red burdah. In Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that the red hullah is an expression for two garments from Yemen with red and green stripes, not that it is pure red, so the wearing of the burdah should be interpreted as one of them.' End quote. This is based on evidence of his prohibition of wearing pure red as narrated by Abu Dawud, and the statement takes precedence over the action, and the prohibiting evidence is given precedence over the permitting evidence if they conflict, so how about when they do not conflict under the aforementioned interpretation? And he added in al-Hawi al-Qudsi that among the recommended acts are adornment, showing joy and cheerfulness, and giving much charity according to one's ability. And he added in al-Qunyah the desirability of wearing a ring, early rising (tabkir), which is quick awakening and going early to the prayer place, praying Fajr in his neighborhood mosque, going out walking to the prayer place, returning via a different route, greeting with the words 'May Allah accept from us and from you' which is not objectionable. And in al-Mujtaba: 'If you say: Ghusl is counted here as recommendatory (mustahab) while in the chapter of Taharah it is Sunnah, I say: There is a difference of opinion on it, and the correct is that it is Sunnah, and he called it mustahab because Sunnah includes mustahab, and other recommended acts mentioned here are counted in some books as Sunnah.' End quote.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the recommended acts (mundubat) for the day of Eid al-Fitr according to the Hanafi school. It begins by quoting the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which enumerates five acts: eating (before the prayer), performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, and wearing one's best clothes. All are done in emulation of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary then elaborates: it is mustahabb that the food be sweet, citing the hadith that the Prophet would eat an odd number of dates before leaving for prayer. The practice of mixing dates with milk and breaking the fast on that (if one is fasting) is not from the Sunnah. Regarding clothes, the best should be worn even if not white; the Prophet wore a red burdah, but this is interpreted as a striped garment, not pure red, to avoid contradicting the prohibition of wearing pure red. Additional recommended acts mentioned in other sources include: adorning oneself, showing joy, giving charity, wearing a ring, early rising, going early to the prayer place, praying Fajr in one's neighborhood mosque, walking to the prayer place, returning via a different route, and greeting fellow Muslims with the du'a 'Taqabbala Allahu minna wa minkum.' There is a slight difference in classification: ghusl is called mustahab here but in Taharah it is called Sunnah. The commentator follows the view that it is Sunnah, and the term mustahab is used because Sunnah encompasses mustahab. Other acts are also recorded as Sunnah in some books.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended, rewarded but not obligatory or sinful to omit. Sometimes used interchangeably with sunnah in this text.
تبكير (tabkir): Going early to the prayer place on Eid, rapid awakening.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on eating dates before the Eid prayer?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) because the Prophet did it.
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) and should be odd in number.
C) It is forbidden (haram) because it breaks the fast.
D) It is makruh (disliked) because it is not a confirmed sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school encourages a set of recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr that reflect joy, gratitude, and emulation of the Prophet, with careful reconciliation of evidence as shown in the clothing example.

The Eid Khutbah: Not a Condition, But a Sunnah
Clarifies that the Eid khutbah is not a condition for validity; it is sunnah to be after the prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Eid khutbah and explain why it is not a condition for the validity of the Eid prayer.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is a sunnah after the prayer, not a condition that invalidates if omitted.

This lesson clarifies a common misconception about the Eid prayer. While Jumu'ah requires a sermon as a condition, the Eid prayer does not. The Hanafi school holds that the Eid khutbah is a recommended sunnah that should be performed after the prayer, and its omission or advance does not invalidate the prayer. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct fiqh rulings for Eid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the khutbah (sermon) of the Eid prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not a condition (shart) for the prayer's validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the prophetic practice: the Prophet (peace be upon him) delivered the khutbah after the Eid prayer. Additionally, the principle that a condition must precede or accompany the act supports this.
The text cites al-Nahr and al-Zahiriyyah as sources.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Because the Prophet always performed the khutbah after the prayer, it cannot be a condition, as conditions typically precede or are concomitant. This timing shows it is a sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i school) consider the khutbah a condition. The Hanafi response is that the practice and logical principle confirm it is not.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the khutbah is sunnah. If delivered before the prayer, the prayer is still valid, though it is disliked (makruh tanzih).
Sheikh Ismail explicitly supports this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإنها ليست بشرط أي بل سنة لأنها تؤدى بعد الصلاة وشرط الشيء يسبقه أو يقارنه . كذا في النهر قال: وتأخيرها إلى ما بعد صلاة العيد سنة. كذا في الظهيرية. وهذا يقتضي أنه لو خطب قبلها كان آتياً بأصلها وفيه توقف إذ لم ينقل قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وليس بصحيح لجواز المتقدمة وعدم إعادتها كما وقع بهما التصريح . قوله : (وبه اندفع ما في (السراج أي بما أفاد المصنف أن جميع شرائط الجمعة وجوباً وصحة
His statement: 'For it (the sermon) is not a condition, i.e., rather it is Sunnah, because it is performed after the prayer, and the condition of something precedes it or is concomitant. This is in al-Nahr. He said: 'And delaying it until after the Eid prayer is Sunnah.' Likewise in al-Zahiriyyah. This implies that if he delivered the sermon before the prayer, he would be performing its essential (act), but there is hesitation because it is not transmitted. Sheikh Ismail said: 'And it is not correct because of the permissibility of it being advanced and not repeating it, as is explicitly stated.' His statement: 'And by this is refuted what is in al-Siraj,' i.e., by what the author mentioned that all conditions of Jumuah, in terms of obligation and validity...
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah-style) clarifying the status of the Eid sermon (khutbah) as mentioned in the matn: 'except the sermon.' The commentator explains that the sermon is not a condition for the validity of the Eid prayer; rather, it is sunnah (recommended). Normatively, a condition must precede or accompany the act, but the Eid sermon is performed after the prayer. Delaying it until after the prayer is the established sunnah. If one delivers the sermon before the prayer, it is still valid, although it is considered a sin (isā'ah) because one is leaving the sunnah. This is supported by the explicit statements of the early scholars. The comment also refutes a concern from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj about the obligation of Eid on a slave: since the sermon is not a condition, the analogy with Jumuah fails.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A prerequisite for the validity of the prayer; the sermon is not a shart.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; leaving it without excuse is blameworthy but the prayer remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if one delivers the Eid khutbah before the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but it is disliked (makruh)
C) The prayer is invalid only if done intentionally
D) The khutbah cannot be before the prayer, so the prayer is null

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is not a condition for the prayer's validity; it is a sunnah to be performed after the prayer, and if done before, the prayer remains valid.

Takbir in Eid al-Fitr: Proof, Dispute, and Mufta Bihi
Commentary expanding the prohibition of takbir loudness before Eid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two students on takbir in Eid al-Fitr, explain the Quranic evidence, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Loud takbir in Eid al-Fitr is bid'ah; quiet takbir is allowed but not a prescribed sunnah.

The matn 'غير مكبر' is brief, but the commentary in Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks a rich debate within the Hanafi school. At stake is whether takbir should be recited at all before the Eid al-Fitr prayer, and if so, how. This lesson walks through the textual evidence, the intra-madhhab disagreement, and the practical fatwa on loud and quiet takbir.

Guided Path
1
Understand the matn's surface meaning
The matn says 'without takbir' before the Eid prayer. Apparent meaning: no takbir at all, either loudly or quietly.
This is the starting point for the commentary.
2
Identify the commentator's clarification
The commentator then explains that the prohibition is specifically for loud takbir; quiet takbir is permissible. This clarification is supported by Ghayat al-Bayan.
The distinction between loud and quiet is central.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Khulasah records that Abu Hanifa holds no takbir even quietly, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) allow quiet takbir. This is a major ikhtilaf within the school.
The disagreement is about the origin, not just the manner.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The prohibition of loud dhikr is based on Quran 7:205. Takbir for Eid al-Adha is based on Quran 2:203. No specific proof exists for Eid al-Fitr, so takbir there is not legislated.
The absence of specific evidence makes loud takbir bid'ah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
Later authorities (al-Khulasah, Qadikhan, al-Ayni) uphold that loud takbir is bid'ah (makruh tahrimi). Quiet takbir is makruh tanzihi if intended for Eid, otherwise recommended.
The dominant fatwa follows Abu Hanifa, though some allow quiet takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (غير مكبر ومتنفل (قبلها أي قبل صلاة العيد. أما الأول فظاهر كلامه أنه لا يكبر الفطر قبل صلاة العيد لا جهراً ولا سراً وأنه لا فرق بين التكبير في البيت أو في الطريق أو في المصلي قبل الصلاة لكن أفاد بعد ذلك أن أحكام الأضحى كالفطر إلا أنه يكبر في الطريق جهراً ، فصار معنى كلامه هنا أنه لا يكبر في الطريق جهراً. وفي غاية البيان: المراد من نفي التكبير بصفة الجهر لأن التكبير خير موضوع لا خلاف في جوازه بصفة الإخفاء اهـ. وفي الخلاصة ما يخالفه قال ولا يكبر يوم الفطر وعندهما يكبر ويخافت وهو إحدى الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة والأصح ما ذكرنا أنه لا يكبر في عيد الفطر اهـ. فأفاد أن الخلاف أصله لا في صفته وأن المراد التكبير في هذه الأيام .اهـ. وهو مردود لأن صاحب الخلاصة أعلم بالخلاف منه ولأن ذكر الله تعالى إذا قصد به التخصيص بوقت دون وقت أو بشيء دون شيء لم يكن مشروعاً حيث لم يرد الشرع به لأنه خلاف المشروع، وكلامهم إنما هو فيما إذا خص يوم الفطر بالتكبير ولهذا قال في غاية البيان من باب المهر عند ذكر المتعة : وقوله ولا يكبر في طريق المصلى عند أبي حنيفة أي حكماً للعيد ولكن لو كبر لأنه ذكر الله تعالى يجوز ويستحب . فالحاصل أن الجهر بالتكبير بدعة في كل وقت إلا في المواضع المستثناة. وصرح قاضيخان في فتاواه بكراهة الذكر جهراً وتبعه على ذلك صاحب المستصفى. وفي الفتاوى العلامية وتمنع الصوفيه من رفع الصوت والصفق. وصرح بحرمته العيني في شرح التحفة وشنع على من يفعله مدعياً أنه من الصوفية، واستثنى من ذلك في القنية ما يفعله الأئمة في زماننا فقال : إمام يعتاد في كل غداة مع جماعته قراءة آية الكرسي وآخر البقرة عليه وسلم اهـ . وأما التكبير خفيه فإن قصد أن يكون لأجل يوم الفطر فهو مكروه أيضاً وإلا فهو مستحب ولو كان الفطر.
His statement (without takbir and without supererogatory prayer) before it, meaning before the Eid prayer. As for the first, the apparent meaning of his statement is that he does not recite takbir for al-Fitr before the Eid prayer, neither loudly nor secretly, and that there is no difference between takbir at home, on the way, or in the musalla before the prayer. However, he later indicated that the rulings of al-Adha are like al-Fitr except that one recites takbir on the way loudly. Therefore, the meaning of his statement here is that he does not recite takbir on the way loudly. In Ghayat al-Bayan: what is meant by negating takbir is the quality of loudness, because takbir is a good act; there is no disagreement about its permissibility in a hidden manner. In al-Khulasah, there is something contradicting it: it says he does not recite takbir on the day of al-Fitr, and according to the two companions, he recites it quietly, and it is one of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and the correct is what we mentioned, that he does not recite takbir in Eid al-Fitr. So he indicated that the disagreement is in its origin, not in its description, and that there is agreement on the absence of loudness. Fath al-Qadir rejected this, saying it is nothing, because it prevents mentioning Allah with various words at any time, but rather it is from its occurrence in a manner of bid'ah. Thus Abu Hanifa said: raising the voice in dhikr is bid'ah and contradicts the command of Allah: 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and in fear and without loudness of speech' (al-A'raf 205), so it is confined to what is legislated. And it has been legislated in al-Adha, which is the verse: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' (al-Baqarah 203); in the exegesis, it means takbir in these days. This is refuted because the author of al-Khulasah is more knowledgeable of the disagreement, and because dhikr of Allah when intended for specification of a time or thing is not legislated where not indicated by law, as it is contrary to legislation. Their speech is only about when one specifies the day of al-Fitr with takbir. Hence, in Ghayat al-Bayan, in the chapter of mahr regarding mut'ah, it says: 'His statement: and he does not recite takbir on the way to the musalla according to Abu Hanifa means as a ruling for the Eid, but if he recites takbir because it is the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible and recommended.' The conclusion is that loud takbir is bid'ah at all times except excepted places. Qadikhan explicitly stated in his Fatawa the dislike of dhikr loudly, and the author of al-Mustasfa followed him. In al-Fatawa al-Alamiyyah, they prohibit the Sufis from raising their voice and clapping. Al-Ayni explicitly stated its prohibition in Sharh al-Tuhfah and denounced those who do it claiming to be Sufis. He excepted in al-Qunyah what the imams do in our time: 'An imam who habitually recites Ayat al-Kursi and the end of al-Baqarah and similar things aloud with his congregation in every morning is fine, but hiding is better.' Then he said: 'Loud takbir outside the days of Tashriq is only sunnah when facing the enemy or thieves, and some analogized to it fire and all dangers.' Then he numbered another section: 'A Qadi and with him a large group raising their voices in tahleel and tasbeeh collectively is fine, and hiding is better. If they gather in dhikr, tasbeeh, and tahleel, they should hide, and hiding is better when in fear on a ship or playing with swords, and similarly sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him).' As for quiet takbir, if he intends it for the day of al-Fitr, it is also disliked; otherwise it is recommended, even if it is al-Fitr.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the matn's phrase 'غير مكبر' (without takbir). The commentator explains that the matn's apparent meaning is that one should not recite takbir at all, either loudly or softly, before the Eid prayer for Eid al-Fitr. However, he clarifies that the prohibition is specifically for loud takbir, as quiet takbir is permissible. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that no takbir (even quietly) is prescribed for Eid al-Fitr, while his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow quiet takbir. The commentator discusses various sources and concludes that loud takbir in general is considered bid'ah except in legislated exceptions (e.g., Eid al-Adha, battle). The fatwa literature indicates that quiet takbir is disliked if specifically intended for Eid al-Fitr, but otherwise it is recommended as general dhikr. The passage cites Quranic verses to support the prohibition of loud dhikr (al-A'raf 205) and the specification of takbir in Eid al-Adha (al-Baqarah 203). The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that loud takbir in Eid al-Fitr is not part of the sunnah and is considered bid'ah (makruh tahrimi), while quiet takbir is permissible but makruh tanzihi if done with the intention of Eid.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbīr): Uttering 'Allahu Akbar' as an act of worship.
بدعة (bid‘ah): Innovation in religious matters; here, loud takbir in Eid al-Fitr is considered bid'ah.
جهر (jahr): Loudness; specifically reciting takbir audibly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting takbir loudly in Eid al-Fitr before the prayer?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh tahrimi
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Loud takbir in Eid al-Fitr is bid'ah; quiet takbir is permissible but not a prescribed sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Ruling on Loud Takbir on Eid al-Fitr (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on loud takbir for Eid al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on loud takbir on Eid al-Fitr and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Loud takbir on Eid al-Fitr is makruh according to the preferred Hanafi view, unlike Eid al-Adha.

This lesson examines the ruling on raising the voice in takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) on the day of Eid al-Fitr. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it an innovation (bid'a), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, permit it. The passage from Bahr al-Raiq discusses this ikhtilaf and the evidence from the Quran, highlighting two conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ikhtilaf
Recognize the specific legal question: whether to raise the voice in takbir on Eid al-Fitr. Note that the ikhtilaf is between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.
The dispute is intra-madhhab, not between schools.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa rules that loud takbir is a bid'a. He uses Quran 7:205 (remembrance without loudness) and argues that specific legislation exists only for Eid al-Adha (2:203).
His preferred narration is from al-Mu'alla: no jahr.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow loud takbir. They rely on another narration from Abu Hanifa (via Ibn Abi 'Imran) that permits jahr, and they generalize the verse on Eid al-Adha (2:203) to include Eid al-Fitr.
They also argue that Quran 7:205 is not a prohibition of loud dhikr in all contexts.
4
Analyze the tarjih attempts
Later scholars disagree on which narration from Abu Hanifa is preferred. Al-Khulasa prefers al-Mu'alla (silence), while al-Razi prefers Ibn Abi 'Imran (jahr). The passage does not give a definitive tarjih but notes the difference.
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi congregation, some may say takbir loudly and others quietly.

في عيد الفطر فلا يكبر جهراً في قول أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد يجهر ا هـ. وكذا في السراج الوهاج والتتارخانية ومواهب الرحمن ودرر البحار. وقال في النهر : غير مكبر أي جهراً وهذا رواية المعلي عن الإمام، وروى الطحاوي عن ابن أبي عمران البغدادي عن الإمام أنه يكبر جهراً وهو قولهما، واختلف المشايخ في الترجيح فقال الرازي الصحيح من قول أصحابنا ما رواه ابن أبي عمران، وما رواه المعلى لم يعرف عنه. وفي الخلاصة : الأصح ما رواه المعلى. كذا في الدراية. قال
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers. ... (complete literal translation of the Arabic text above)
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of raising the voice in takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') on the day of Eid al-Fitr. The author begins by citing a view that the original ruling is not about the description but that there is agreement on not being loud, but this is rejected in Fath al-Qadir. Abu Hanifa states that raising the voice in dhikr is an innovation (bid'a) and contradicts the verse 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and fear and without loudness of speech' (Quran 7:205). He argues that the practice should be limited to what is legislated, which is only for Eid al-Adha based on Quran 2:203 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days.' The text then refutes this by saying that the author of al-Khulasa is more knowledgeable about the difference of opinion. It concludes that loud takbir is an innovation except in exceptional circumstances like facing an enemy. The core ikhtilaf is: Abu Hanifa says it is not allowed (or even forbidden), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is permissible (jahr is allowed). The later scholars differ on which transmission from Abu Hanifa is correct: some prefer the narration from Ibn Abi 'Imran that permits jahr, while others prefer the narration from al-Mu'alla that forbids it. The preferred view according to al-Khulasa is the narration of al-Mu'alla (i.e., not loud).

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' on the occasion of Eid.
الجهر (al-jahr): Raising the voice, as opposed to ikhfa (silent or low voice).
بدعة (bid'a): An innovation in religion not based on prophetic practice; here, considered a blameworthy innovation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Quran 2:203
B) Quran 7:205
C) Quran 1:1
D) Quran 112:1

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two narrations on loud takbir for Eid al-Fitr; the preferred view is that it is not done loudly.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayer Before and After Eid Prayer
Commentary on the ruling of supererogatory prayer before and after the Eid prayer, with exceptions for the common people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayer before and after the Eid prayer and distinguish when it is disliked and when it is recommended, with evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer before Eid is disliked only in the musalla; at home it is allowed, and after Eid it is recommended at home.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on supererogatory prayers around the Eid prayer. The author reconciles conflicting hadith by distinguishing between the prayer ground (musalla) and home, and also provides a leniency for the common people to encourage worship. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the principle that location and context can affect the legal ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what is being discussed: voluntary prayer (nafl) before and after the Eid prayer. The ruling is: it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to pray nafl before Eid in the musalla; at home it is not disliked. After Eid, it is recommended to pray at home (preferably four rak'ahs).
Distinguish between musalla and home.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ﷺ did not pray before or after Eid in the musalla, and the hadith from Ibn Majah that he prayed two rak'ahs after returning home. Clarify that the negation of after prayer applies only to the musalla.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The hadiths are reconciled by interpreting the Prophet's action: his not praying in the musalla indicates dislike, while his praying at home indicates recommendation. The negation in the first hadith is specific to the musalla, as shown by the second hadith.
This uses the Hanafi principle of reconciling apparent contradictions by specifying context (takhsis).
4
Note the exception for the common people
The author adds that common people should not be prevented from offering takbir or even praying Fajr late, because forbidding them might lead them to abandon worship entirely. This is based on the principle of avoiding hardship and preserving people's engagement in religion.
This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) based on maqasid.
5
Evaluate practical application
The ruling means that on Eid day, one should avoid praying any nafl in the open prayer ground before the Eid prayer. After the Eid prayer, it is better to go home and pray four rak'ahs (or two). Women who want to pray Duha should do so after the imam finishes in the musalla. Other schools may allow nafl before Eid; the Hanafi school considers it makruh tanzihi.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between schools.

Source Text

فلما
Two rak'ahs, two by two before the additional [takbirs] and they are three in each rak'ah, and he continues between the two recitations and raises his hands in ... the prayer place, it is disliked according to the generality, but if at home then no. The evidence for dislike is what is in the six books from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet [ﷺ] went out and prayed Eid with them, he did not pray before it nor after it. And this negation of after it is interpreted as being in the prayer place because of the hadith of Ibn Majah: the Messenger of Allah [ﷺ] would not pray anything before Eid, and when he returned to his home he prayed two rak'ahs. He said in Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa: and it is better to pray four rak'ahs after it, and it is general, including the Duha prayer, and including whoever prayed Eid, imam or otherwise, and whoever did not pray it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And for this in al-Khulasa: women who want to pray Duha on Eid day pray after the imam prays in the musalla. All this is according to the situation of a person, but the common people are not prevented from takbir before it. Abu Ja'far said: the common people should not be prevented from that due to their lack of desire for good deeds. Similarly for voluntary prayer before it. He said in al-Tajnisa: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani was asked about lazy commoners who pray Fajr at sunrise, should we forbid them? He said: No, because if they are prevented they will leave it entirely, and performing it with the permissibility of the people of hadith is better than leaving it entirely.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding voluntary prayer before and after the Eid prayer. The text first gives the ruling that it is disliked (makruh) to pray nafl before the Eid prayer when in the musalla (prayer ground). If one is at home, it is not disliked. The evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet did not pray before or after the Eid prayer when he led it in the musalla. However, the hadith from Ibn Majah clarifies that the negation of after prayer applies only to the musalla, because when the Prophet returned home he prayed two rak'ahs. Therefore, after the Eid prayer, it is recommended to pray at home. Some scholars say it is better to pray four rak'ahs, which can be the Duha prayer. For the common people, however, they should not be prevented from engaging in acts of worship like takbir or even praying Fajr late, because preventing them might lead them to abandon the act altogether. This is based on the principle of taking the easier option to keep them engaged in religion.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer.
المصلى (al-musalla): The designated prayer ground for Eid, typically an open area outside the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the prayer ground (musalla) and home for voluntary prayers on Eid, and supports leniency for the common people to maintain their engagement in worship.

Time of Eid Prayer and Its Conditions
Commentary on the time of Eid prayer from sunrise to zenith, with proofs and special rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time of Eid prayer in the Hanafi madhhab and explain the legal implications of praying before or after this time.

Core Idea
The time for Eid prayer is limited to the forenoon; praying outside this window invalidates the prayer.

This lesson examines the precise timing of Eid prayer according to Hanafi fiqh. The time is defined from after sunrise (approximately a spear's height) until the sun's zenith. We will see the Prophetic proofs for this ruling and the consequences of praying outside this time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Eid prayer, which is a sunnah muakkadah. Its time is a condition (shart) for validity.
2
Locate the dalil for the beginning time
The hadith states that the Prophet prayed Eid when the sun was at a spear's height or two.
This gives a lower bound of about 15-20 minutes after sunrise.
3
Locate the dalil for the ending time
The hadith of the group testifying to the moon: the Prophet ordered them to go to the musalla the next morning, indicating the prayer must be before zenith.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
If the prayer were valid after zenith, there would be no need to specify the next morning. The order implies the prayer must be performed in the forenoon.
5
Note the special ruling on fasad
If the sun passes its zenith during the prayer, it becomes invalid (fasid), just like Jumu'ah.
This is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ووقتها من ارتفاع الشمس إلى (زوالها أما الابتداء فلأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي العيد والشمس على قيد رمح أو رمحين، وهو بكسر القاف بمعنى قدر. وأما الانتهاء في السنن أن ركباً جاؤوا إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يشهدون أنهم رأوا الهلال بالأمس فأمرهم أن يفطروا إذا أصبحوا يغدون إلى مصلاهم، ولو جاز فعلها بعد الزوال لم يكن للتأخير إلى الغد معنى. واستفيد منه أنها لا تصح قبل ارتفاع الشمس بمعنى لا تكون صلاة عيد بل نفل محرم. ولو زالت الشمس وهو في أثنائها فسدت كما في الجمعة. صرح به في السراج الوهاج. وعلى هذا فينبغي إدخاله في المسائل الإثني عشرية لما أنها كالجمعة وقد أغفلوها عن ذكرها. ويستحب تعجيل صلاة الأضحى لتعجيل الأضاحي. وفي المجتبى : ويستحب أن يكون خروجه بعد ارتفاع قدر رمح حتى لا يحتاج إلى انتظار القوم، وفي عيد الفطر يؤخر الخروج قليلاً. كتب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى عمرو بن حزم عجل الأضحى وأخر الفطر. قيل: ليؤدي الفطرة ويعجل الأضحية. قوله ( ويصلى ركعتين مثنيا قبل الزوائد) أما كونها ركعتين فمتفق عليه وأما كون الثناء قبل التكبيرات فلأنه شرع أول الصلاة فيقدم عليها في الرواية كما يقدم على سائر الأفعال والأذكار قوله (وهي ثلاث في كل ركعة) أي الزوائد

His saying: 'And its time is from the rising of the sun to its zenith.' As for the beginning, because the Prophet [ﷺ] used to pray Eid when the sun was at the height of a spear or two spears, which is with a kasra on the qaf meaning measure. As for the end, in the Sunan that a group came to the Prophet [ﷺ] testifying that they saw the crescent yesterday, so he ordered them to break their fast and go to their musalla the next morning. If it were permissible after zenith, delaying until the next day would have no meaning. It is derived that it is not valid before sunrise, meaning it would not be an Eid prayer but rather a forbidden voluntary prayer. And if the sun passes its zenith while he is in the midst of it, it becomes invalid, just as in Jumu'ah. This is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And accordingly, it should be included among the twelve issues because it is like Jumu'ah, and they have neglected to mention it. It is recommended to hasten the Eid al-Adha prayer to hasten the sacrifice. And in al-Mujtaba: it is recommended that his going out be after the height of a spear so that he does not need to wait for the people, and on Eid al-Fitr he delays exiting a little. The Prophet [ﷺ] wrote to 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'Hasten the Adha and delay the Fitr.' It is said: to pay the fitra and hasten the sacrifice. His saying: 'And he prays two rak'ahs two by two before the additional [takbirs]' as for it being two rak'ahs, it is agreed upon. As for the thana' before the takbirs, because it is legislated at the beginning of the prayer, it is presented before them in the narration just as it is presented over all other actions and remembrances. His saying: 'And they are three in each rak'ah' meaning the additional. It appears that al-Razi and our shaykhs beyond the river. So the dispute is regarding jahr and its absence as stated in al-Tajnis, and upon this flowed Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Sharh. And likewise flowed Mukhtarat al-Nawazil and the commentators of al-Hidaya, and he attributed it in al-Nihaya to al-Mabsut and Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' and Zad al-Fuqaha'. The author's saying: 'And its time is from the rising of the sun' said the commentator al-Zayla'i: the meaning of rising is that it becomes white [i.e., the sun brightens]...
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Eid prayer. The beginning of the time is after sunrise by about one or two spear lengths (approx. 15-20 minutes after sunrise) because that is when the Prophet prayed. The end of the time is before zenith (midday). This is proven by the hadith of a group who testified seeing the moon, so the Prophet ordered them to break their fast (i.e., it was Eid) and go to the musalla the next morning. If Eid prayer were valid after zenith, there would be no reason to delay. Therefore, if one starts the prayer and the sun passes zenith during it, the prayer becomes invalid, similar to Jumu'ah. The text also mentions that it is recommended to hasten the Eid al-Adha prayer to allow for the sacrifice, while on Eid al-Fitr it is recommended to delay slightly to allow people to pay fitra. The later part of the passage returns to the description of the prayer structure (two rak'ahs, extra takbirs) and then discusses a dispute about jahr (loudness) again, linking back to the earlier takbir discussion.

Key Terms
قيد رمح (qayd ramh): A measure of length approximately the height of a spear, used to estimate the time after sunrise (about 15-20 minutes).
الزوال (al-zawal): The zenith, i.e., the moment the sun passes its meridian and begins to decline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer becomes invalid (fasid) and must be repeated

D) The prayer becomes a voluntary prayer

Key Takeaway
The time for Eid prayer is strictly from after sunrise to before zenith; deviation invalidates the prayer.

Ruling on Optional Prayers Before and After Eid
States the ruling on optional prayers before and after Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayers before and after the Eid prayer and distinguish between the musalla and home contexts based on the prophetic practice.

Core Idea
Nafl before/after Eid is disliked in the musalla but recommended at home.

This lesson examines the ruling on optional (nafl) prayers surrounding the Eid prayer. While many assume that no nafl is allowed at all, the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between location: the musalla (open prayer ground) and one's home. You will learn the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the practical application of this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is performing optional (nafl) prayers immediately before or after the Eid prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that this is disliked (makruh tanzih) when done in the musalla, but not disliked at home; in fact, it is recommended to pray four rak'ahs after returning home.
The ruling applies to both before and after Eid, but the evidence focuses on after.
2
Locate the dalil
Two key hadiths are cited: (1) Ibn Abbas (ra) narrates that the Prophet (saw) did not pray before or after Eid in the musalla. (2) Ibn Majah's hadith adds that when the Prophet returned home, he would pray two rak'ahs.
These hadiths are from the six books and are considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The negation in the first hadith ('did not pray') is interpreted as indicating dislike in the musalla, because the second hadith shows prayer at home. Thus, the prohibition is location-specific.
Hanafi usul: a negation of an action by the Prophet can indicate prohibition or dislike depending on context.
4
Note the exception and ta'lil
The exception is that at home, nafl is not only permissible but recommended (four rak'ahs after Eid). This is supported by later Hanafi authorities like Qadikhan and al-Khulasa.
The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the Prophet's action at home establishes the sunna there.
5
Apply the ruling to common scenarios
The ruling applies to everyone: imam, ma'mum, and even those who missed the Eid prayer. Women praying Duha on Eid day should wait until after the imam finishes in the musalla. Common people should not be prevented from performing takbeer or nafl before Eid, as this might discourage them entirely.
This is based on fiqh principles of ease and encouraging the common people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة العيدين
ركعتين مثنياً قبل الزوائد وهي ثلاث في كل ركعة ويوالي بين القراءتين ويرفع يديه في المصلي فمكروه عند العامة، وإن كان في البيت فلا ودليل الكراهة ما في الكتب الستة عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي الله يخرج فصلى بهم العيد لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها. وهـذا الـنـفـي بـعـدهـا محمول على ما إذا كان في المصلى لحـديـث ابـن مـاجـه قـال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يصلي قبل العيد شيئاً فإذا رجع إلى منزله صلى ركعتين اهـ. قال في فتاوى قاضيخان والخلاصة : والأفضل أن يصلي أربع ركعات .بعدها وأطلقه فشمل صلاة الضحى وشمل من يصلي صلاة العيد إماماً كان أو غيره ومن لم يصلها كما في السراج الوهاج ولهذا في الخلاصة : : النساء إذا أردن أن يصلين صلاة الضحى يوم العيد صلين بعدما يصلي الإمام في الجبانة اهـ. وهذا كله إنما هو بحسب حال الإنسان، وأما العوام فلا يمنعون من تكبير قبلها . قال أبو جعفر : لا ينبغي أن يمنع العامة من ذلك لقلة رغبتهم في الخيرات اهـ . وكذا في التنفل قبلها . قال في التجنيس : سئل شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن كسالى العوام يصلون الفجر عند طلوع الشمس أفنزجرهم عن ذلك؟ قال : لا لأنهم إذا منعوا عن ذلك تركوها أصلاً وأداؤها مع تجويز أهل الحديث لها أولى من تركها أصلاً اهـ.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers: Two rak'ahs with praise before the additional [takbeers], and they are three in each rak'ah, and he recites consecutively between the two recitations, and he raises his hands. [Praying] in the musalla is disliked (makruh) according to the general scholars, but if at home then not. The evidence for the dislike is what is in the six books from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would go out and pray the Eid with them [and] did not pray before it nor after it. And this negation after it is interpreted as when it is in the musalla, due to the hadith of Ibn Majah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not pray anything before Eid, and when he returned to his home, he would pray two rak'ahs. It is said in the Fatawa of Qadikhan and al-Khulasa: It is better to pray four rak'ahs after it. And it is absolute, so it includes the Duha prayer and includes whoever prays the Eid prayer, whether imam or other, and whoever did not pray it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And for this, in al-Khulasa: If women wish to pray the Duha prayer on the day of Eid, they pray after the imam prays in the open space (al-jabbana). All this is according to the situation of the person. As for the common people, they are not prevented from takbeer before it. Abu Ja'far said: One should not prevent the common people from that due to their lack of desire for good deeds. Similarly for optional prayer before it. It is said in al-Tajnis: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani was asked about lazy common people who pray Fajr at sunrise; should we prevent them? He said: No, because if they are prevented from that, they would leave it entirely, and performing it with the permissibility of the people of hadith is better than leaving it entirely.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the ruling on performing optional (nafl) prayers before and after the Eid prayer. The author begins by stating that praying nafl in the musalla (the designated out-of-town prayer ground) before or after the Eid prayer is disliked (makruh) according to most scholars. However, if one prays at home, it is not disliked. This ruling is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas (recorded in the six canonical hadith collections) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer when he led it in the musalla. The negative after it is interpreted specifically for the musalla, because of the hadith from Ibn Majah which states that when the Prophet returned home, he would pray two rak'ahs. Thus, the prohibition is limited to the musalla. The author then cites Fatawa Qadikhan and al-Khulasa, which state that it is preferable to pray four rak'ahs after the Eid prayer (presumably at home). This ruling applies generally to anyone who prays the Eid prayer, including the imam and others, and extends to the Duha prayer. For example, if women wish to pray Duha on Eid day, they should wait until after the imam prays in the open space. The passage also addresses the case of common people ('awamm). It is not appropriate to prevent them from performing takbeer (i.e., reciting takbirat) before the Eid prayer, nor from performing nafl prayers at that time, because they have little enthusiasm for good deeds. This is illustrated by the response of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: if lazy common people pray Fajr at sunrise (after its preferred time), they should not be prevented, because forbidding them would lead them to abandon it entirely, and praying it with the legal permissibility (according to some hadith scholars) is better than complete abandonment.

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The open area outside the town designated for the Eid prayer.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, optional prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
تكبير (takbeer): The recitation of 'Allahu Akbar' which is done before the Eid prayer, as part of the general practice on Eid days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying two rak'ahs of nafl in the musalla before the Eid prayer?
A) It is recommended (mandub).
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is obligatory (wajib).
D) It is permissible (mubah).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, praying optional prayers before or after Eid in the musalla is disliked (makruh tanzih), but praying them at home is recommended.

Time of the Eid Prayer
Specifies the time for the Eid prayer from sunrise until zenith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for the Eid prayer, identify the evidence for its beginning and end, and apply the ruling when the time expires during the prayer.

Core Idea
The Eid prayer time is from sunrise (height of a spear) to zenith; praying outside this window invalidates the Eid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq specifies the time conditions for the Eid prayer. We learn that the prayer must be performed after the sun has risen approximately a spear's height and before the sun reaches its zenith. The author supports this with prophetic practice and a hadith. Understanding this time condition is essential for the validity of the Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the beginning time
Look at the phrase 'من ارتفاع الشمس' and the evidence from the Prophet's practice of praying when the sun was at the height of a spear.
ارتفاع الشمس means the sun has risen enough to be about a spear's height above the horizon.
2
Identify the ending time
The text states 'إلى زوالها' (to its zenith) and supports this with the hadith of the riders who were ordered to go to the musalla the next morning.
If praying after noon were valid, there would be no reason to delay until the next day.
3
Understand the consequence of missing the time
If the sun passes the zenith during the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid), analogous to the Friday prayer.
This is explicitly stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
4
Note additional recommendations
The text recommends hastening the Eid al-Adha prayer and delaying the Eid al-Fitr prayer based on a letter from the Prophet to Amr ibn Hazm.
The reason is to allow for sacrifice and fitra respectively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ووقتها من ارتفاع الشمس إلى (زوالها أما الابتداء فلأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي العيد والشمس على قيد رمح أو رمحين، وهو بكسر القاف بمعنى قدر. وأما الانتهاء في السنن أن ركباً جاؤوا إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يشهدون أنهم رأوا الهلال بالأمس فأمرهم أن يفطروا إذا أصبحوا يغدون إلى مصلاهم، ولو جاز فعلها بعد الزوال لم يكن للتأخير إلى الغد معنى. واستفيد منه أنها لا تصح قبل ارتفاع الشمس بمعنى لا تكون صلاة عيد بل نفل محرم. ولو زالت الشمس وهو في أثنائها فسدت كما في الجمعة. صرح به في السراج الوهاج. وعلى هذا فينبغي إدخاله في المسائل الإثني عشرية لما أنها كالجمعة وقد أغفلوها عن ذكرها. ويستحب تعجيل صلاة الأضحى لتعجيل الأضاحي. وفي المجتبى : ويستحب أن يكون خروجه بعد ارتفاع قدر رمح حتى لا يحتاج إلى انتظار القوم، وفي عيد الفطر يؤخر الخروج قليلاً. كتب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى عمرو بن حزم عجل الأضحى وأخر الفطر. قيل: ليؤدي الفطرة ويعجل الأضحية.
His saying (and its time is from the rising of the sun to its zenith). As for the beginning, it is because he (peace and blessings be upon him) used to pray the Eid while the sun was at the height of a spear or two spears – with a kasra on the qaf meaning 'measure'. As for the end, it is in the Sunan that a group of riders came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) testifying that they had seen the crescent the previous day, so he ordered them to break their fast and when morning came to go to their musalla. And if performing it after zenith were permissible, there would be no point in delaying it to the next day. From this it is understood that it is not valid before the sun has risen, meaning it would not be an Eid prayer but rather a forbidden nafl. And if the sun passes the zenith while he is in the midst of it, it becomes invalid (fasid), just like in the Friday prayer. This is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Accordingly, it should be included among the twelve issues because it is like the Friday prayer, and they have omitted it. It is recommended to hasten the Eid al-Adha prayer to expedite the slaughter. In al-Mujtaba: It is recommended that his departure be after the height of a spear so that he does not need to wait for the people, and on Eid al-Fitr he delays departure a little. The Prophet (peace be upon him) wrote to Amr ibn Hazm: 'Hasten the Adha and delay the Fitr.' It is said: to perform the fitra and expedite the sacrifice.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the time for the Eid prayer, which is a key ruling for validity. The author begins by referencing the matn that states the time is from sunrise (when the sun has risen the height of a spear) to the zenith (zawal). For the beginning time, the evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray the Eid prayer when the sun was at the height of a spear or two, i.e., approximately 15 to 30 minutes after actual sunrise. For the end time, the author cites the hadith in the Sunan: a group of riders came to the Prophet testifying that they had seen the moon for Eid the previous evening, and he ordered them to break their fast and go out the next morning to the musalla. If the Eid prayer could be performed after noon, there would be no reason to delay it to the next day. Hence, the end time is the zenith. If the sun passes the zenith while one is still in the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid), analogous to the Friday prayer. The author notes that this case should be included among the twelve issues (where parallels between Eid and Friday are drawn), but earlier works omitted it. The passage also discusses the recommendation to hasten the Eid al-Adha prayer to allow time for the sacrifice, and to delay the Eid al-Fitr prayer slightly to allow for distribution of fitra. This is based on a letter from the Prophet to Amr ibn Hazm.

Key Terms
ارتفاع الشمس (irtifa' al-shams): The sun having risen to the height of a spear (approx. 15-30 minutes after sunrise), marking the beginning of the Eid prayer time.
زوال (zawal): The sun's crossing the zenith, i.e., the meridian; marks the end of the Eid prayer time.
رمح (rumh): A spear; used as a measure of the sun's height above the horizon at the time of the Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the sun passes its zenith while a person is in the middle of the Eid prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
B) The prayer remains valid but is disliked.
C) The prayer becomes a nafl prayer.
D) The person must repeat the prayer after noon.

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer must be performed after sunrise (when the sun is a spear's height) and before the sun reaches its zenith; otherwise the prayer is not valid as an Eid prayer.

Number of Extra Takbeers in Eid Prayer: Three or Five?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbeer count with resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of extra takbeers in the Eid prayer and explain why Abu Yusuf's practice of five does not contradict the madhhab.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab holds three extra takbeers; the caliphal order of five was followed externally, not doctrinally.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key issue in Hanafi fiqh: the number of extra takbeers in the Eid prayer. While the school's position is three, a historical incident involving Imam Abu Yusuf and Caliph Harun al-Rashid created a temporary practice of five. Understanding why this does not change the madhhab is crucial for proper fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the school's position
Recognize that the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) adopts the view of Ibn Mas'ud: three extra takbeers in each rak'ah.
This is the mufta bihi and the most authentic narration (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Recognize the opposing view
Ibn Abbas transmitted five or four takbeers. The Abbasid caliphs ordered the public to follow this, leading to a conflict.
This is a legitimate companion difference, not a rejection of sunnah.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's action
When Abu Yusuf led the Eid prayer in Baghdad with Harun al-Rashid, he used the five-takbeer formula. This was compliance with the caliph's order, not a change in his own madhhab.
Obedience to the ruler in non-prohibited matters is wajib, but it does not alter one's fiqh position.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position remains three. However, when the imam uses more, the congregation follows as long as it does not exceed sixteen.
The caliphal order was temporary; now the original madhhab is revived.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويصلى ركعتين مثنيا قبل الزوائد) أما كونها ركعتين فمتفق عليه وأما كون الثناء قبل التكبيرات فلأنه شرع أول الصلاة فيقدم عليها في الرواية كما يقدم على سائر الأفعال والأذكار قوله (وهي ثلاث في كل ركعة) أي الزوائد ظاهر الرازي وعليه مشايخنا بما وراء النهر. فالخلاف في الجهر وعدمه كما صرح به في التجنيس وعليه جرى في غاية البيان والشرح .ا.هـ. وكذا جرى عليه في مختارات النوازل وشراح الهداية وعزاه في النهاية إلى المبسوط وتحفة الفقهاء وزاد الفقهاء .
قول المصنف : ( ووقتها من ارتفاع الشمس قال الشارح الزيلعي : المزاد بالارتفاع أن تبيض
عن ثلاث تكبيرات في كل ركعة وهو قول ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه وبه أخذ أئمتنا أبو حنيفة وصاحباه. وأما ما في الخلاصة وعن أبي يوسف كما قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما خمس الأولى وخمس في الثانية أو أربع على اختلاف الروايات والأئمة في زماننا يكبرون عل مذهب ابن عباس لأن الخلفاء شرطوا عليهم ذلك .اهـ. فليس مذهباً لأبي يوسف وإنما فعله امتثالاً لأمر هرون الرشيد قال في السراج الوهاج لما انتقلت الولاية إلى بني العباس أمروا الناس بالعمل في التكبيرات بقول جدهم وكتبوا ذلك في مناشيرهم. وهذا تأويل ما روي أبي يوسف أنه قدم بغداد فصلى بالناس صلاة العيد وخلفه هرون الرشيد فكبر تكبير ابن عباس، فيحتمل أن هرون أمره أن يكبر تكبير جده ففعله امتثالاً لأمره، وأما مذهبه فهو على تكبير ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه لأن التكبير ورفع الأيدي خلاف المعهود فكان الأخذ فيه بالأقل أولى اهـ. وكذا هو مروي عن محمد قال في الظهيرية : إنهما فعلا ذلك امتثالاً لأمر الخليفة لا مذهباً ولا اعتقاداً وذكر في المجتبى ثم يأخذ بأي هذه التكبيرات شاء، وفي رواية عن أبي يويسف ومحمد قال في الموطأ بعد ذكر الروايات فما أخذت به فحسن، ولو كان فيها ناسخ ومنسوخ لكان محمد بن الحسن أولى بمعرفته لقدمه في علم الحديث والفقه. وقيل : الآخر ناسخ للأول والصحيح ما قلناه والأخذ بتكبيرات ابن مسعود أولى اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أن الخلاف في الأولوية. وفي المحيط : ولو كبر الإمام أكثر من تكبير ابن مسعود اتبعه ما لم يكبر أكثر مما جاء به الآثار لأنه مولى عليه فيلزمه العمل برأي الإمام وذلك إلى ستة عشر، فإن زاد لا يلزمه متابعته لأنه مخطئ بيقين. ولو سمع التكبيرات من المكبرين يأتي بالكل احتياطاً وإن كثر لاحتمال الغلط من المكبرين ولهذا قيل : ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح لاحتمال
قوله: (ففعله امتثالاً لأمره لأن طاعة الإمام فيما ليس بمعصية واجبة وهذا ليس بمعصية لأنه قول بعض الصحابة كذا في المعراج وقال في شرح المنية : والذي ذكروا من عمل العامة بقول ابن عباس لأمر بينه الخلفاء بذلك كان في زمنهم، أما في زماننا فقد زال إذ لا خليفة الآن، والذي يكون بمصر فهو خليفة اسماً لا معنى لانتفاء بعض شروط الخلافة فيه على ما لا يخفى على من له أدنى علم بشروطها، فالعمل الآن بما هو المذهب عندنا لكن حيث لا يقع الالتباس على الناس ا هـ. أقول : هذا أن أمر الخليفة بشيء لا يبقى حكمه بعد موته أو عزله إذ لو بقي العمل بأمره واجباً لوجب علينا إلى اليوم العمل بما أمر به هرون أبا يوسف وبه يعلم حكم أوامر سلاطين بني عثمان فتدبر قوله : (ولهذا قيل ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح الخ) أقول : ظاهره أنه ينوي بما زاد على الستة عشر لأنه الذي ظهر به احتمال الغلط ولعل وجهه أنه لما زاد على المأثور احتمل خطأ المكبرين بأنهم زادوا تكبيرة مثلاً، واحتمل أن تكون هذه الزائدة هي تكبيرة الافتتاح تقدموا بها على الإمام فلم يصح الشروع فلذا ينوي بما زادوه الافتتاح.
يؤخذ من
His saying (and he prays two rak'ahs with praise before the extras). As for their being two rak'ahs, it is agreed upon. As for the praise before the takbeers, it is because it is prescribed at the beginning of the prayer, so it precedes them in the narration just as it precedes all other actions and remembrances. His saying (and they are three in each rak'ah) meaning the extras is apparent in al-Razi, and our scholars beyond the river follow that. The disagreement is about whether it is aloud or not, as made clear in al-Tajnis, and this is followed in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Sharh. Similarly in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil and the commentators of al-Hidayah, and it is attributed in al-Nihaya to al-Mabsut, Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', and Ziyadat al-Fuqaha'. The author's saying: (and its time from sunrise) al-Zayla'i said: by sunrise it means when it becomes white. About three takbeers in each rak'ah, and that is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). Our imams Abu Hanifa and his two companions adopted it. As for what is in al-Khulasa and from Abu Yusuf, it is like what Ibn Abbas said: five in the first and five in the second, or four according to different narrations, and the imams in our time say takbeer according to the madhhab of Ibn Abbas because the caliphs imposed that upon them. So this is not a madhhab of Abu Yusuf; rather he did it in compliance with the order of Harun al-Rashid. It is said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When rule passed to the Abbasids, they ordered the people to act according to the saying of their grandfather (Ibn Abbas) and wrote that in their decrees. This is the interpretation of what was narrated from Abu Yusuf: he came to Baghdad and led the people in the Eid prayer with Harun al-Rashid behind him, and he said the takbeer of Ibn Abbas. It is possible that Harun ordered him to say the takbeer of his grandfather, so he did it in compliance with his order. As for his madhhab, it is upon the takbeer of Ibn Mas'ud because takbeer and raising the hands depart from the usual, so taking the lesser is better. And this is also narrated from Muhammad. It is said in al-Zahiriyya: They both did that in compliance with the order of the caliph, not as a madhhab or belief. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba: Then one may take whichever of these takbeers he wishes. In a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is said in al-Muwatta after mentioning the narrations: Whatever you take is good, and if there were abrogating and abrogated, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan would be more qualified to know it due to his precedence in hadith and fiqh. It is said: The latter abrogates the former, but the correct is what we said, and adopting the takbeer of Ibn Mas'ud is better. Thus it becomes clear that the disagreement is about preference. In al-Muhit: If the imam says takbeer more than that of Ibn Mas'ud, follow him as long as he does not exceed what has been narrated in the traditions, because he is responsible [for the prayer] and it is necessary to follow his opinion. That is up to sixteen. If he adds more, it is not necessary to follow him because he is definitely mistaken. And if one hears the takbeers from the muballighs, he should perform them all out of precaution, even if many, due to the possibility of error from the muballighs. For this reason, it is said: He should intend with every takbeer the opening, because of the possibility. His saying: (He did it in compliance with his order because obedience to the imam in what is not disobedience is obligatory, and this is not disobedience because it is the saying of some companions) as in al-Mi'raj. And in Sharh al-Munyah: What they mentioned about the general public acting according to the saying of Ibn Abbas due to the caliphs' order was in their time. As for our time, it has ceased since there is no caliph now. The one in Egypt is a caliph in name only without meaning due to some conditions of the caliphate being absent, as is not hidden from one who has the least knowledge of its conditions. So now the practice is according to our madhhab, but only where it does not cause confusion among the people. I say: This means that the order of the caliph concerning something does not continue after his death or removal. If it were obligatory to act upon his order, we would be obliged to this day to act upon what Harun ordered Abu Yusuf. With this the ruling of the orders of the Ottoman sultans is known, so ponder. His saying: (For this it is said he intends with every takbeer the opening) I say: Its apparent meaning is that he intends with those above sixteen because that is where the possibility of error appears. Perhaps the reason is that when he exceeds the narrated number, it is possible that the muballighs made a mistake, e.g., they added a takbeer, and it is possible that this extra is the opening takbeer which they preceded the imam with, so the start was not valid. Therefore, he intends with what they added the opening. Taken from
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed discussion on the number of extra takbeers (takbirat zawa'id) in the Eid prayer, a central issue in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by noting that the matn states the prayer is two rak'ahs with praise before the extra takbeers, and that the extra takbeers are three in each rak'ah. This is the view of Ibn Mas'ud (ra) and is the adopted madhhab of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage also mentions a conflicting view attributed to Ibn Abbas (ra), who transmitted five takbeers in the first rak'ah and five in the second, or four according to some narrations. The author explains that the Abbasid caliphs, particularly Harun al-Rashid, ordered the imams to follow the practice of their ancestor (Ibn Abbas), and thus Abu Yusuf, when he led the Eid prayer in Baghdad with the caliph behind him, complied by using the five-takbeer formula. This was not his actual madhhab; rather, it was an act of obedience to the caliph's command, which is not sinful since it is based on a companion's opinion. The author clarifies that the dispute is one of preference (awlawiyya), not of validity. In practice, the later Hanafi scholars state that if the imam uses more than three takbeers, the congregation should follow him as long as he does not exceed what is narrated in traditions (up to sixteen). If the imam exceeds sixteen, he is definitively mistaken, and following him is not required. A further issue arises when one hears the takbeers from the muballighs (those who call out the takbeers) and is unsure of the count: to be cautious, one should perform all takbeers heard, intending with each the opening takbeer in case of doubt. The passage concludes with a discussion on the authority of the caliph's order, noting that it was limited to their time; in later eras without a true caliph, the original madhhab should be followed, provided it does not confuse the laity.

Key Terms
تكبيرات زوائد (takbirat zawa'id): The extra takbeers in the Eid prayer beyond the opening takbeer, recited in each rak'ah.
مكبر (muballigh (plural muballighun)): The person who loudly conveys the takbeer of the imam to the congregation.
تكبيرة الافتتاح (takbirat al-iftitah): The opening takbeer that begins the prayer; one intends with each extra takbeer the possibility of it being the opening if in doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the relied-upon number of extra takbeers in the Eid prayer?
A) Five
B) Three
C) Four
D) Two

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab holds three extra takbeers as the preferred and mufta bihi, but allows following the imam if he uses a different number up to sixteen.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Following the Imam and Precautionary Takbeers in Eid Prayer
Ruling on following the imam and precautionary intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that the congregation must follow the imam's extra takbeers up to sixteen, and explain the precaution of intending the opening takbeer when counts are uncertain.

Core Idea
Follow the imam up to sixteen extra takbeers; beyond that, he is mistaken. When in doubt, intend the opening takbeer.

After clarifying the number of extra takbeers, the text addresses practical scenarios: what if the imam uses more than three? And how should one act when hearing takbeers from multiple muballighs? These rulings ensure orderly prayer while maintaining the school's principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of following the imam
The imam is responsible for the prayer; the congregation must follow him in actions as long as they are within the shariah.
Obedience is wajib unless the imam commits a clear error.
2
Identify the maximum limit of sixteen
Based on transmitted traditions, the imam may be followed up to sixteen extra takbeers. If he exceeds, he is definitely mistaken and should not be followed.
This limit ensures the prayer remains valid.
3
Apply the precaution when hearing muballighs
If one hears takbeers from helpers and is unsure of the count, he should perform all takbeers out of caution, intending that each could be the opening takbeer.
This resolves the doubt about the proper start of prayer.
4
Understand the rationale for the opening takbeer intention
When extra takbeers are heard, one may have missed the actual opening takbeer. By intending every takbeer as opening, precaution is taken.
This is a legal stratagem (hila) to ensure validity.

Source Text

عن ثلاث تكبيرات في كل ركعة وهو قول ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه وبه أخذ أئمتنا أبو حنيفة وصاحباه. وأما ما في الخلاصة وعن أبي يوسف كما قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما خمس الأولى وخمس في الثانية أو أربع على اختلاف الروايات والأئمة في زماننا يكبرون عل مذهب ابن عباس لأن الخلفاء شرطوا عليهم ذلك .اهـ. فليس مذهباً لأبي يوسف وإنما فعله امتثالاً لأمر هرون الرشيد قال في السراج الوهاج لما انتقلت الولاية إلى بني العباس أمروا الناس بالعمل في التكبيرات بقول جدهم وكتبوا ذلك في مناشيرهم. وهذا تأويل ما روي أبي يوسف أنه قدم بغداد فصلى بالناس صلاة العيد وخلفه هرون الرشيد فكبر تكبير ابن عباس، فيحتمل أن هرون أمره أن يكبر تكبير جده ففعله امتثالاً لأمره، وأما مذهبه فهو على تكبير ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه لأن التكبير ورفع الأيدي خلاف المعهود فكان الأخذ فيه بالأقل أولى اهـ. وكذا هو مروي عن محمد قال في الظهيرية : إنهما فعلا ذلك امتثالاً لأمر الخليفة لا مذهباً ولا اعتقاداً وذكر في المجتبى ثم يأخذ بأي هذه التكبيرات شاء، وفي رواية عن أبي يويسف ومحمد قال في الموطأ بعد ذكر الروايات فما أخذت به فحسن، ولو كان فيها ناسخ ومنسوخ لكان محمد بن الحسن أولى بمعرفته لقدمه في علم الحديث والفقه. وقيل : الآخر ناسخ للأول والصحيح ما قلناه والأخذ بتكبيرات ابن مسعود أولى اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أن الخلاف في الأولوية. وفي المحيط : ولو كبر الإمام أكثر من تكبير ابن مسعود اتبعه ما لم يكبر أكثر مما جاء به الآثار لأنه مولى عليه فيلزمه العمل برأي الإمام وذلك إلى ستة عشر، فإن زاد لا يلزمه متابعته لأنه مخطئ بيقين. ولو سمع التكبيرات من المكبرين يأتي بالكل احتياطاً وإن كثر لاحتمال الغلط من المكبرين ولهذا قيل : ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح لاحتمال
قوله: (ففعله امتثالاً لأمره لأن طاعة الإمام فيما ليس بمعصية واجبة وهذا ليس بمعصية لأنه قول بعض الصحابة كذا في المعراج وقال في شرح المنية : والذي ذكروا من عمل العامة بقول ابن عباس لأمر بينه الخلفاء بذلك كان في زمنهم، أما في زماننا فقد زال إذ لا خليفة الآن، والذي يكون بمصر فهو خليفة اسماً لا معنى لانتفاء بعض شروط الخلافة فيه على ما لا يخفى على من له أدنى علم بشروطها، فالعمل الآن بما هو المذهب عندنا لكن حيث لا يقع الالتباس على الناس ا هـ. أقول : هذا أن أمر الخليفة بشيء لا يبقى حكمه بعد موته أو عزله إذ لو بقي العمل بأمره واجباً لوجب علينا إلى اليوم العمل بما أمر به هرون أبا يوسف وبه يعلم حكم أوامر سلاطين بني عثمان فتدبر قوله : (ولهذا قيل ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح الخ) أقول : ظاهره أنه ينوي بما زاد على الستة عشر لأنه الذي ظهر به احتمال الغلط ولعل وجهه أنه لما زاد على المأثور احتمل خطأ المكبرين بأنهم زادوا تكبيرة مثلاً، واحتمل أن تكون هذه الزائدة هي تكبيرة الافتتاح تقدموا بها على الإمام فلم يصح الشروع فلذا ينوي بما زادوه الافتتاح.

His saying (and he prays two rak'ahs with praise before the extras). As for their being two rak'ahs, it is agreed upon. As for the praise before the takbeers, it is because it is prescribed at the beginning of the prayer, so it precedes them in the narration just as it precedes all other actions and remembrances. His saying (and they are three in each rak'ah) meaning the extras is apparent in al-Razi, and our scholars beyond the river follow that. The disagreement is about whether it is aloud or not, as made clear in al-Tajnis, and this is followed in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Sharh. Similarly in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil and the commentators of al-Hidayah, and it is attributed in al-Nihaya to al-Mabsut, Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', and Ziyadat al-Fuqaha'. The author's saying: (and its time from sunrise) al-Zayla'i said: by sunrise it means when it becomes white. About three takbeers in each rak'ah, and that is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). Our imams Abu Hanifa and his two companions adopted it. As for what is in al-Khulasa and from Abu Yusuf, it is like what Ibn Abbas said: five in the first and five in the second, or four according to different narrations, and the imams in our time say takbeer according to the madhhab of Ibn Abbas because the caliphs imposed that upon them. So this is not a madhhab of Abu Yusuf; rather he did it in compliance with the order of Harun al-Rashid. It is said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When rule passed to the Abbasids, they ordered the people to act according to the saying of their grandfather (Ibn Abbas) and wrote that in their decrees. This is the interpretation of what was narrated from Abu Yusuf: he came to Baghdad and led the people in the Eid prayer with Harun al-Rashid behind him, and he said the takbeer of Ibn Abbas. It is possible that Harun ordered him to say the takbeer of his grandfather, so he did it in compliance with his order. As for his madhhab, it is upon the takbeer of Ibn Mas'ud because takbeer and raising the hands depart from the usual, so taking the lesser is better. And this is also narrated from Muhammad. It is said in al-Zahiriyya: They both did that in compliance with the order of the caliph, not as a madhhab or belief. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba: Then one may take whichever of these takbeers he wishes. In a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is said in al-Muwatta after mentioning the narrations: Whatever you take is good, and if there were abrogating and abrogated, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan would be more qualified to know it due to his precedence in hadith and fiqh. It is said: The latter abrogates the former, but the correct is what we said, and adopting the takbeer of Ibn Mas'ud is better. Thus it becomes clear that the disagreement is about preference. In al-Muhit: If the imam says takbeer more than that of Ibn Mas'ud, follow him as long as he does not exceed what has been narrated in the traditions, because he is responsible [for the prayer] and it is necessary to follow his opinion. That is up to sixteen. If he adds more, it is not necessary to follow him because he is definitely mistaken. And if one hears the takbeers from the muballighs, he should perform them all out of precaution, even if many, due to the possibility of error from the muballighs. For this reason, it is said: He should intend with every takbeer the opening, because of the possibility. Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Number of Takbirs in Eid Prayer: Hanafi Position
Establishes the Hanafi ruling of three takbirs per rak'ah in Eid prayer, following Ibn Mas'ud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of takbirs in Eid prayer and explain why the disagreement is one of preference (awlawiyya) rather than validity.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds three takbirs per rak'ah in Eid prayer, following Ibn Mas'ud; other counts are permissible but less preferred.

In Eid prayers, there are additional takbirs besides the regular ones, but scholars differ on how many. The Hanafi school follows the narration of Ibn Mas'ud that there are three per rak'ah, while some early reports from Ibn Abbas mention five or four. This lesson explains the Hanafi position and shows that apparent differences in practice, like that of Imam Abu Yusuf, were due to external factors, not a change in doctrine. The core of the dispute is about which number is more virtuous (awlawiyya), not about validity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the number of takbirs per rak'ah in Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school. The passage explicitly states: three takbirs per rak'ah, following Ibn Mas'ud, and that this is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing view and its source
The passage mentions the report of Ibn Abbas: five takbirs in the first rak'ah and five in the second, or four, as an alternative narration. This practice was adopted by the Abbasid caliphs who commanded the imams to act accordingly.
The opposing view is not attributed to a specific school but to a Companion's narration and caliphal decree.
3
Explain the apparent intra-Hanafi contradiction
A report exists that Abu Yusuf, when leading Eid prayer in Baghdad with Harun al-Rashid, performed the takbirs according to Ibn Abbas (five or four). The passage clarifies this was done in obedience to the caliph's command, not as his personal madhhab. Similarly, Muhammad al-Shaybani is reported to have done the same.
The key is that acts done under compulsion or orders do not reflect the scholar's own considered opinion.
4
Analyze the nature of the disagreement
The passage concludes that the difference is about awlawiyya (preference), not about validity. Either set of takbirs can be used, but three is considered more appropriate because takbir and raising hands is 'contrary to the customary' (khilaf al-ma'hud), so the lesser number is taken. This is a preference, not a ruling of obligation.
This is seen in the quote: 'Whatever you adopt, it is good.'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical result is that a Hanafi who prays Eid with an imam who uses five takbirs, or who follows the Abbasid practice, has a valid prayer. However, the more virtuous (afdal) practice according to the Hanafi school is three takbirs per rak'ah.
This understanding prevents unnecessary conflict and allows for flexibility in congregational settings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From three takbirs in every rak'ah — that is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him), and our imams Abu Hanifa and his two companions took it. As for what is in al-Khulasa and from Abu Yusuf, as Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: five in the first and five in the second, or four, according to variance of narrations — and the imams in our time perform takbirs according to the school of Ibn Abbas because the caliphs imposed that upon them. End. So it is not a madhhab for Abu Yusuf; rather he did it in compliance with the command of Harun al-Rashid. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: When the caliphate transferred to the Banu Abbas, they ordered people to act regarding the takbirs according to the saying of their grandfather, and wrote that in their decrees. This is the interpretation of what was narrated from Abu Yusuf: that he came to Baghdad and led the people in Eid prayer with Harun al-Rashid behind him, and he performed the takbir of Ibn Abbas. It is possible that Harun ordered him to perform the takbir of his grandfather, so he did it in compliance with his command. As for his madhhab, it is upon the takbir of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) because takbir and raising hands is contrary to the customary, so taking the lesser is more appropriate. End. Similarly, it is narrated from Muhammad; he said in al-Zahiriyya: They both did that in compliance with the caliph's command, not as a madhhab nor as belief. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba: Then he may adopt any of these takbirs he wishes. In a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, he said in al-Muwatta after mentioning the narrations: Whatever you adopt is good. And if there were abrogating and abrogated, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan would be more deserving of its knowledge due to his precedence in the science of hadith and fiqh. And it was said: The latter abrogates the former, but the correct is what we said, and adopting the takbirs of Ibn Mas'ud is more appropriate. End. With this it appears that the disagreement is about preference.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the number of takbirs in Eid prayer. The Hanafi school follows the position of Ibn Mas'ud: three takbirs in each rak'ah. The passage clarifies that Abu Yusuf's reported practice of using five or four takbirs (following Ibn Abbas) was not his actual madhhab; he did so under the caliph's command. The author explains that the disagreement is about preference (awlawiyya), not about validity. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that since takbir and raising hands is not a firmly established practice, the lesser number is taken as a precaution. The passage also notes that later scholars in the time of the Abbasids were ordered to follow Ibn Abbas's count due to caliphal decree.

Key Terms
التكبيرات (al-takbirat): The additional takbirs (Allahu Akbar) recited in the Eid prayer beyond the regular takbirs of the prayer
أولوية (awlawiyya): Preference; the disagreement is not about validity but about which practice is more virtuous
خلاف المعهود (khilaf al-ma'hud): Contrary to the customary or established norm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred number of takbirs in each rak'ah of the Eid prayer?
A) Five
B) Four
C) Three
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds three takbirs per rak'ah in Eid prayer as the preferred practice, and the disagreement with other narrations is about preference (awlawiyya), not validity.
