Following the Imam in Eid Takbirs and the Muballigh's Role
Ruling on following the imam's takbirs and precaution with the muballigh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following the imam in Eid takbirs and apply the precaution regarding the muballigh's repetition.

Core Idea
Follow the imam’s Eid takbirs up to sixteen; beyond that, the imam is clearly wrong.

The Eid prayer includes extra takbirs beyond the normal prayer. A key question is how many takbirs the follower should perform with the imam, especially if the imam adds more. This passage from al-Muhit clarifies the limit and explains the precautionary approach when a muballigh repeats the takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal ruling on the follower's participation in the imam's takbirs. The extra takbirs are sunnah mu'akkadah, but the follower is obligated to follow the imam's count as long as it does not exceed the reported maximum.
The ruling is based on obedience to the imam in non-disobedient matters.
2
Establish the limit: sixteen takbirs
The traditions report a maximum of sixteen takbirs (including the opening takbir). If the imam does more than sixteen, he is clearly mistaken, and the follower is not obligated to follow.
This limit is from the practice of Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Understand the precaution with the muballigh
If the follower hears takbirs from the muballigh (the person who repeats the imam's takbirs for the congregation), he should perform all of them as a precaution, because the muballigh might have made an error (e.g., added a takbir or started before the imam).
The precaution includes intending the opening takbir with each takbir to ensure validity if an error occurred.
4
Analyze the rationale behind the precaution
The possibility of error from the muballigh is the basis for the instruction to perform all takbirs heard. This ensures that if the muballigh mistakenly started with the opening takbir before the imam, the follower's prayer remains valid.
This is a pragmatic safeguard, not an obligation to exceed the limit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : ولو كبر الإمام أكثر من تكبير ابن مسعود اتبعه ما لم يكبر أكثر مما جاء به الآثار لأنه مولى عليه فيلزمه العمل برأي الإمام وذلك إلى ستة عشر، فإن زاد لا يلزمه متابعته لأنه مخطئ بيقين. ولو سمع التكبيرات من المكبرين يأتي بالكل احتياطاً وإن كثر لاحتمال الغلط من المكبرين ولهذا قيل : ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح لاحتمال. قوله: (ففعله امتثالاً لأمره لأن طاعة الإمام فيما ليس بمعصية واجبة وهذا ليس بمعصية لأنه قول بعض الصحابة كذا في المعراج وقال في شرح المنية : والذي ذكروا من عمل العامة بقول ابن عباس لأمر بينه الخلفاء بذلك كان في زمنهم، أما في زماننا فقد زال إذ لا خليفة الآن، والذي يكون بمصر فهو خليفة اسماً لا معنى لانتفاء بعض شروط الخلافة فيه على ما لا يخفى على من له أدنى علم بشروطها، فالعمل الآن بما هو المذهب عندنا لكن حيث لا يقع الالتباس على الناس ا هـ. أقول : هذا أن أمر الخليفة بشيء لا يبقى حكمه بعد موته أو عزله إذ لو بقي العمل بأمره واجباً لوجب علينا إلى اليوم العمل بما أمر به هرون أبا يوسف وبه يعلم حكم أوامر سلاطين بني عثمان فتدبر قوله : (ولهذا قيل ينوي بكل تكبيرة الافتتاح الخ) أقول : ظاهره أنه ينوي بما زاد على الستة عشر لأنه الذي ظهر به احتمال الغلط ولعل وجهه أنه لما زاد على المأثور احتمل خطأ المكبرين بأنهم زادوا تكبيرة مثلاً، واحتمل أن تكون هذه الزائدة هي تكبيرة الافتتاح تقدموا بها على الإمام فلم يصح الشروع فلذا ينوي بما زادوه الافتتاح.
And in al-Muhit: If the imam did more takbirs than the takbirs of Ibn Mas'ud, the follower should follow him as long as he does not exceed what has been reported in the traditions, because he is under his authority and must act according to the imam's opinion, up to sixteen. If he exceeds, the follower is not obligated to follow him because he is definitely mistaken. And if he hears the takbirs from the muballighs (those who repeat the takbirs), he should come with all of them as a precaution, even if many, due to the possibility of error from the muballighs. For this reason it was said: He should intend the opening takbir with each takbir due to possibility. His saying: (He did it in compliance with his command because obedience to the imam in what is not disobedience is obligatory, and this is not disobedience because it is the saying of some companions. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And he said in Sharh al-Munya: What they mentioned that the common people act on the saying of Ibn Abbas due to the caliphs' order was in their time. As for our time, it has ceased, as there is no caliph now. The one in Egypt is a caliph in name only, meaning not, due to the absence of some conditions of the caliphate, as is not hidden from anyone with minimal knowledge of its conditions. So the practice now is according to our madhhab, but only where confusion does not occur among the people. End. I say: This is that the caliph's command regarding something does not remain effective after his death or removal, for if acting on his command were obligatory, we would be obliged until today to act on what Harun ordered Abu Yusuf. By this the ruling of the commands of the Ottoman sultans is known, so ponder. His saying: (And for this reason it was said: He should intend the opening takbir with each takbir) I say: Its apparent meaning is that he intends with what exceeds sixteen, because the possibility of error appears in that. Perhaps its reasoning is that when it exceeds the reported number, it is possible the muballighs made an error, for example adding a takbir, and it is possible that this extra is the opening takbir which they preceded the imam with, so the commencement (of prayer) was not valid; therefore he intends the opening with what they added.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on following the imam in Eid takbirs. If the imam does more than three takbirs, the follower must follow him as long as the imam does not exceed sixteen takbirs – the maximum reported in traditions. Beyond sixteen, the imam is clearly wrong and should not be followed. When hearing takbirs from the muballigh (the person who repeats the imam's takbirs for the congregation), the follower should perform all the takbirs they hear as a precaution, because the muballigh might err. In such a case, it is recommended to intend the opening takbir with each takbir they perform, to ensure that if the muballigh mistakenly started with the opening takbir before the imam, the follower's prayer is valid. The commentary adds that the command of the caliph to follow Ibn Abbas's count was specific to that time; now that there is no true caliph, the Hanafi madhhab should be followed.

Key Terms
المكبرين (al-mukabbirin): Those who repeat the takbirs of the imam for the congregation (muballighs)
تكبير ابن مسعود (takbir Ibn Mas'ud): The practice of the companion Ibn Mas'ud regarding the number of takbirs in Eid prayer, which is a reference for the maximum of sixteen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) Seven
C) Sixteen
D) Unlimited

Key Takeaway
Follow the imam's Eid takbirs up to sixteen; beyond that, stop following, and when a muballigh repeats takbirs, perform all heard as a precaution.

Rulings for the Individual Follower and Latecomer in Eid Prayer Takbirs
Rulings on how the individual follower and the latecomer should perform the takbirs in Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the individual follower and the latecomer in performing Eid takbirs, and apply the principle of following one's own opinion versus the imam's opinion.

Core Idea
The individual follows his own opinion for takbirs; the follower follows his imam; the latecomer makes up missed takbirs according to his own opinion.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the key principles for performing the extra takbirs in Eid prayer, distinguishing between the individual (munfarid), the follower (muqtadi), and the latecomer (masbuq). You will learn when to say the takbirs in ruku' and when not to, and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Recognize the three roles: munfarid (praying alone), muqtadi (following an imam), and masbuq (latecomer who missed part of the prayer).
The ruling for each is different regarding the takbirs.
2
Apply the basic principle
The munfarid follows his own opinion about the number of takbirs; the muqtadi follows his imam's opinion; the masbuq follows his own opinion for the missed takbirs when making them up.
This principle guides all subsequent scenarios.
3
Analyze the scenario of catching the imam in ruku'
If the masbuq catches the imam in ruku' and fears the imam will rise, he should bow and say the takbirs in ruku' according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf who holds he should say them before bowing.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Determine rulings for other situations
If the follower catches the imam standing but the imam bows before the follower says the takbirs, the follower should not say them in ruku'. Similarly, if the imam forgets the takbirs before bowing, he does not make them up in ruku' nor returns to standing. The latecomer who misses the first part should say his missed takbirs immediately when starting his qada'.
These complete the practical scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤخذ من التقدم على الإمام في كل تكبيرة .اهـ. ثم قال : الأصل أن المنفرد يتبع رأي نفسه في التكبيرات والمقتدي يتبع رأي إمامه، ومن أدرك الإمام راكعاً في صلاة العيد فخشي أن يرفع رأسه يركع ويكبر في ركوعه عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، ولو أدركه في القيام فلم يكبر حتى ركع لا يكبر في الركوع على الصحيح كما لو ركع الإمام قبل أن يكبر فإن الإمام لا يكبر في الركوع ولا يعود إلى القيام ليكبر في ظاهر الرواية، ومن فاتته أول الصلاة مع الإمام يكبر في الحال ويكبر برأي نفسه .
It is taken from the precedence over the imam in every takbir. End. Then he said: The principle is that the individual follower follows his own opinion regarding the takbirs, and the muqtadi (follower behind an imam) follows the opinion of his imam. And whoever catches the imam bowing in Eid prayer and fears that he will raise his head, he should bow and perform the takbirs in his bowing according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. And if he catches him standing and did not say the takbirs until he bowed, he should not say the takbirs in the bowing according to the correct view, just as if the imam bowed before saying the takbirs, then the imam does not say the takbirs in the bowing nor returns to standing to say them in the apparent narration. And whoever misses the beginning of the prayer with the imam should say the takbirs immediately and follow his own opinion.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings for the individual follower (munfarid) and the latecomer (masbuq) in Eid prayer. The principle is: an individual praying alone follows his own opinion about the number of takbirs, while a follower behind an imam follows the imam's opinion. If a follower joins the imam in ruku', he should bow and say the takbirs in ruku' (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf has a different view). If he catches the imam standing but doesn't say the takbirs until the imam bows, he should not say them in ruku'; similarly, if the imam himself forgets the takbirs before bowing, he does not make them up in ruku' nor returns to standing. The latecomer who misses part of the prayer with the imam should say his missed takbirs immediately when he starts making up the rak'ah, according to his own opinion.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the congregation late and misses part of the prayer, including some takbirs
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, not behind an imam
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): A person praying behind an imam in congregation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Say the takbirs before bowing
D) Skip the takbirs

Key Takeaway
In Eid prayer, the individual follower relies on his own opinion; the follower behind an imam follows the imam; the latecomer makes up missed takbirs according to his own judgment, and if he catches the imam in ruku', he says the takbirs in ruku' per the relied view.

Muwalat in Eid Takbirs and the Masbuq's Order
Rulings on muwalat, masbuq order, and hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended order for the masbuq in Eid prayer and explain why raising hands is only for the extra takbirs.

Core Idea
The Eid takbirs should be consecutive; the masbuq recites first, then says takbirs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the method of performing the extra takbirs in Eid prayer. It addresses the sequence of actions for both the imam and the masbuq, and resolves an apparent contradiction regarding returning to standing for forgotten takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on muwalat
The passage states that muwalat (consecutiveness) between the extra takbirs is recommended, not obligatory. The term 'obligation' in the source texts means confirmation.
This is based on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and the desire to make the takbirs prominent symbols.
2
Apply the masbuq's procedure
A masbuq (one who missed a rak'ah) should first recite al-Fatihah and a surah, then say the extra takbirs. Starting with takbirs would make the takbirs consecutive without recitation, which was not the practice of the Companions.
The masbuq follows his own opinion for his missed takbirs, unlike the lahiq who follows the imam.
3
Determine the ruling on raising hands
Raising hands is only done for the extra takbirs of Eid, not for the bowing takbir. This is specified because the earlier general statement 'Do not raise hands except in Faq'as Samaj' was ambiguous.
The bowing takbir is considered obligatory (wajib) and forgetting it requires sajdah sahw.
4
Resolve the contradiction on forgotten takbirs
If the imam forgets the extra takbirs before bowing, he does not return to make them up. This is consistent with the case of qunut: qunut is only prescribed in pure standing, so if forgotten in bowing, one does not return.
The author sides with the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) over the view of al-Karkhi, affirming no return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويوالى بين القراءتين) اقتداء بابن مسعود رضي الله عنه ولتكون التكبيرات مجتمعة لأنها من أعلام الشريعة، ولذلك وجب الجهر بها والجمع يحقق معنى الشعائر والإعلام هذا إلا أن في الركعة الأولى تخللت الزوائد بين تكبيرة الافتتاح وتكبيرة الركوع فوجب الضم إلى تكبيرة الافتتاح أولى لأنها سابقة، وفي الركعة الثانية الأصل فيه تكبيرة الركوع لا غيره فوجب الضم إليها ضرورة. كذا في المحيط والهداية . والظاهر أن المراد بالوجوب في عبارتهما الثبوت لا المصطلح عليه لأن الموالاة بينهما مستحبة لما تقدم من أن الخلاف في الأولوية . ثم المسبوق بركعة إذا قام إلى القضاء فإنه يقرأ ثم يكبر لأنه لو بدأ بالتكبير يصير موالياً بين التكبيرات ولم يقل به أحد . الصحابة. ولو بدأ بالقراءة يصير فعله موافقاً لقول علي فكان أولى . كذا في المحيط وهو مخصص لقولهم إن المسبوق يقضي أول صلاته في حق الأذكار ويكبر المسبوق على رأي نفسه بخلاف اللاحق فإنه يكبر على رأي إمامه لأنه خلف الإمام حكماً. كذا في السراج الوهاج . قوله ( ويرفع يديه في الزوائد) توضيح لما أبهمه سابقاً بقوله : ولا يرفع الأيدي إلا في «فقعس صمعج». فإن العين الأولى للإشارة إلى العيدين فبين هنا أنه خاص بالزوائد دون تكبيرة الركوع فإن تكبيرتي الركوع لما ألحقت بالزوائد في كونهما واجبتين حتى يجب السهو بتركهما ساهياً كما صرح به في قوله : (كما لو ركع الإمام الخ هذا مخالف لما ذكره في باب الوتر والنوافل من أنه يكبر في الركوع، وذكر هناك الفرق بينه وبين القنون إذا تذكره في الركوع حيث لا يعود إليه لأن القنوت لم يشرع إلا في محض القيام ومخالف لما في شرح المنية من أنه يعود إلى القيام ويكبر وتكلف للفرق بينه وبين القنوت فإنه على هذا القول يشكل أكثر منه على الأول، وأمنا على ما هنا فلا فرق بينهما فلا إشكال أصلاً، وما هنا صرح بمثله ابن أمير حاج في شرح المنية حيث قال : وإن تذكر في الركوع ففي ظاهر الرواية لا يكبر ويمضي على صلاته، وعلى ما ذكره الكرخي ومشى عليه صاحب البدائع
His saying: (And he makes muwalat between the two recitations) following Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) and so that the takbirs are collected, because they are from the symbols of the Shariah, therefore the loudness is required, and collection achieves the meaning of rituals and announcement. Except that in the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs are inserted between the opening takbir and the bowing takbir, so attaching them to the opening takbir is more appropriate because it comes first. In the second rak'ah, the basis is the bowing takbir, nothing else, so attachment to it is necessary. Thus in al-Muhit and al-Hidayah. The apparent meaning of 'obligation' in their expressions is confirmation, not the technical term, because muwalat between them is recommended since the disagreement is about preference. Then the one who is a rak'ah behind (masbuq) when he stands to make up the rak'ah, he should recite then say the takbirs, because if he starts with the takbirs he would be making consecutive takbirs, which no one among the companions said. And if he starts with recitation, his action agrees with the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), so it is more appropriate. Thus in al-Muhit, and it specifies their saying that the masbuq makes up the first part of his prayer regarding remembrances, and the masbuq says takbirs according to his own opinion, unlike the one who catches up (lahiq) who says takbirs according to the imam's opinion, because he is behind the imam as a ruling. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His saying: (And he raises his hands in the extras) is a clarification of what he previously left ambiguous by his saying: And he does not raise his hands except in 'Faq'as Samaj'. For the first letter indicates the two Eids, so he explains here that it is specific to the extras, not the bowing takbir. For the two bowing takbirs, when they are attached to the extras in that they are both obligatory, so that sahw is required for leaving them forgetfully, as he clarified in his saying: (As if the imam bowed) This is contrary to what he mentioned in the chapter on witr and supererogatory prayers, that he says takbirs in bowing, and he mentioned there the difference between it and qunut when he remembers it in bowing, where he does not return to it because qunut is only prescribed in pure standing. And it contradicts what is in Sharh al-Munya, that he returns to standing and says takbirs, and there is forced difference between it and qunut, for this statement is more problematic than the first. But according to what is here, there is no difference between them, so no problem. And what is here is stated similarly by Ibn Amir Hajj in Sharh al-Munya where he said: If he remembers in bowing, then in the apparent narration he does not say takbirs and proceeds with his prayer, and according to what al-Karkhi mentioned and the author of al-Bada'i followed
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage covers several points: First, the takbirs should be performed consecutively (muwalat) to emphasize them as symbols of Islam. In the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs should be attached to the opening takbir; in the second, to the bowing takbir. The term 'obligation' here means confirmation, not a strict requirement, as muwalat is recommended. Second, a masbuq (one who missed a rak'ah) should first recite al-Fatihah and a surah, then say the takbirs, following the practice of Ali, not starting with takbirs. The masbuq follows his own opinion for his missed takbirs, while the one who catches up (lahiq) follows the imam's opinion. Third, raising hands is only done for the extra takbirs of Eid, not for the bowing takbir. The passage then discusses a contradiction: if the imam forgets the takbirs before bowing, he does not return to make them up; this is like the case of forgetting qunut. The author resolves that there is no difference and no problem, as per the apparent narration.

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Performing the takbirs consecutively without interruption or separation by recitation
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the prayer late and has missed one or more rak'ahs.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): A person who catches up with the imam from the beginning but is delayed in some actions.
الزوائد (al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs in Eid prayer beyond the bowing takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Return to standing, say the takbirs, and then bow again
B) Continue with his prayer and not return
C) Perform sajdah sahw immediately
D) Restart the prayer

Key Takeaway
The masbuq in Eid prayer recites first, then says the extra takbirs; the imam does not return for forgotten takbirs.

Latecomer in Eid Prayer: Takbir in Ruku' and Following One's Opinion
Ruling on latecomer's takbir in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' during Eid prayer and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A latecomer makes takbir in ruku' to join; the imam does not if he forgets.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario in Eid prayer: what should a latecomer do if he catches the imam already in ruku'? The text establishes a general principle about following one's own opinion in the extra takbirs and then presents the ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this helps you navigate the subtle obligations of the latecomer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The passage begins: the munfarid (one praying alone) follows his own opinion in the takbirs, while the muqtadi (follower) follows the imam's opinion. This sets the foundation for the latecomer's role.
The latecomer (masbuq) is considered a munfarid for the part he makes up.
2
Analyze the Latecomer Finding Imam in Ruku'
If the latecomer catches the imam in ruku' and fears the imam will raise his head before he can join, he should bow and make the takbir while in ruku'. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two).
The takbir is performed in ruku' to avoid missing the rak'ah.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that the latecomer should not make takbir in ruku'. The text indicates the relied-upon position is that of the two.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
4
Understand the Exception for Catching Imam Standing
If the latecomer catches the imam standing but delays the takbir until after the imam bows, he does not make takbir in ruku'. This is analogous to the imam himself who forgot: the imam does not return to standing to make it.
This follows the 'apparent transmission' (zahir al-riwaya).
5
Apply to Latecomer Missing the Beginning
Whoever misses the beginning of the prayer with the imam makes the takbir immediately upon joining and follows his own opinion in the number of takbirs.
This reaffirms the principle that the masbuq is like a munfarid for his missed part.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : الأصل أن المنفرد يتبع رأي نفسه في التكبيرات والمقتدي يتبع رأي إمامه، ومن أدرك الإمام راكعاً في صلاة العيد فخشي أن يرفع رأسه يركع ويكبر في ركوعه عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف، ولو أدركه في القيام فلم يكبر حتى ركع لا يكبر في الركوع على الصحيح كما لو ركع الإمام قبل أن يكبر فإن الإمام لا يكبر في الركوع ولا يعود إلى القيام ليكبر في ظاهر الرواية، ومن فاتته أول الصلاة مع الإمام يكبر في الحال ويكبر برأي نفسه .
Then he said: The principle is that the one praying alone follows his own opinion in the takbirs, and the follower follows the opinion of his imam. Whoever catches the imam in ruku' in Eid prayer and fears that he will raise his head, he should bow and make takbir while in ruku' according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. If he catches him while standing and does not make takbir until he has bowed, he does not make takbir in ruku' according to the correct position, just as if the imam bowed before making takbir, then the imam does not make takbir in ruku' nor does he return to standing to make takbir in the apparent transmission. Whoever misses the beginning of the prayer with the imam makes takbir immediately and makes takbir according to his own opinion.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage addresses rulings specific to the latecomer (masbuq) in the Eid prayer. It first establishes the general principle that the one praying alone (munfarid) follows his own opinion regarding the extra takbirs, while the follower (muqtadi) follows the opinion of his imam. Then it discusses specific cases: If a latecomer finds the imam in ruku' and fears the imam will raise his head from ruku' before he can join, he should bow and make the takbir while in ruku'. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two, 'anhuma), while Abu Yusuf disagrees. If the latecomer catches the imam standing but delays the takbir until after the imam has bowed, he does not make takbir in ruku' according to the correct position, analogous to the imam himself who forgot to make the takbir before bowing: the imam does not make takbir in ruku' nor does he return to standing to make it, according to the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya). Finally, if someone misses the entire first part of the prayer with the imam, he makes the takbir immediately upon joining and follows his own opinion in the number of takbirs.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): One who prays alone, not following an imam.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
مسبوق (masbuq): Someone who joins the prayer after the imam has already started, having missed part of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He should wait until the imam stands and then make takbir.
B) He should make takbir while bowing and join the imam in ruku'.
C) He should not make takbir at all.
D) He should return to standing after making takbir.

Key Takeaway
In Eid prayer, a latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' should make the takbir while bowing to join the congregation, following the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Sequence of Recitation and Takbirs in Eid Prayer
Ruling on the order of recitation and takbirs in each rak'ah of Eid prayer and for the latecomer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the recommended sequence of recitation and extra takbirs in each rak'ah of Eid prayer and apply the ruling for a latecomer.

Core Idea
The extra takbirs attach to the nearest obligatory takbir; a latecomer recites first then makes takbir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the proper order of recitation and extra takbirs in the Eid prayer. It clarifies why the takbirs are attached differently in the first and second rak'ahs, and provides important guidance for the latecomer who missed a rak'ah. The ruling balances following the Companions' practice (Ibn Mas'ud and Ali) with the flexibility needed when a person changes their ijtihad or makes an error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule of muwalat
The text states that the two recitations (in the two rak'ahs) should be consecutive. Determine the rationale: following Ibn Mas'ud and gathering the takbirs as symbols of Islam. Note that 'obligatory' here means 'established' (thubut), not the technical wajib.
The actual ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
2
Understand the attachment principle in each rak'ah
In the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs occur between the opening takbir and the ruku' takbir, so they are attached to the opening takbir. In the second rak'ah, the next obligatory takbir after the opening is the ruku' takbir, so they are attached to it.
This explains why the number of takbirs and their placement vary between rak'ahs.
3
Distinguish the latecomer from the lahiq
A latecomer (masbuq) who missed one rak'ah, when standing to make it up, should recite first (after his own opening takbir) and then make the extra takbirs. This follows the opinion of Ali and avoids making the takbirs consecutive without recitation between them. Contrast with the lahiq who follows the imam's opinion on the number of takbirs.
The latecomer follows his own ijtihad regarding the number of takbirs, unlike the lahiq.
4
Handle cases of forgetfulness or change of opinion
If the imam or worshipper errs in the order (e.g., recites before takbirs or vice versa), the text gives rules: if they have not finished the act they entered into, they should correct it; if finished, they continue. Similarly, if one changes their ijtihad (e.g., from Ibn Mas'ud's takbir count to Ibn Abbas's), they follow rules for repeating recitation or continuing based on whether they completed the recitation.
This shows the Hanafi approach to managing errors and changing opinions within the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويوالى بين القراءتين) اقتداء بابن مسعود رضي الله عنه ولتكون التكبيرات مجتمعة لأنها من أعلام الشريعة، ولذلك وجب الجهر بها والجمع يحقق معنى الشعائر والإعلام هذا إلا أن في الركعة الأولى تخللت الزوائد بين تكبيرة الافتتاح وتكبيرة الركوع فوجب الضم إلى تكبيرة الافتتاح أولى لأنها سابقة، وفي الركعة الثانية الأصل فيه تكبيرة الركوع لا غيره فوجب الضم إليها ضرورة. كذا في المحيط والهداية . والظاهر أن المراد بالوجوب في عبارتهما الثبوت لا المصطلح عليه لأن الموالاة بينهما مستحبة لما تقدم من أن الخلاف في الأولوية . ثم المسبوق بركعة إذا قام إلى القضاء فإنه يقرأ ثم يكبر لأنه لو بدأ بالتكبير يصير موالياً بين التكبيرات ولم يقل به أحد . الصحابة. ولو بدأ بالقراءة يصير فعله موافقاً لقول علي فكان أولى . كذا في المحيط وهو مخصص لقولهم إن المسبوق يقضي أول صلاته في حق الأذكار ويكبر المسبوق على رأي نفسه بخلاف اللاحق فإنه يكبر على رأي إمامه لأنه خلف الإمام حكماً. كذا في السراج الوهاج . وفي المجتبى : الأصل أن من قدم المؤخر أو أخر المقدم ساهياً أو اجتهاداً فإن كان لم يفرغ مما دخل فيه يعيد وإن فرغ لا يعود اهـ. وفي المحيط : إن بدأ الإمام بالقراءة سهواً ثم تذكر، فإن فرغ من قراءة الفاتحة والسورة يمضي في صلاته، وإن لم يقرأ إلا الفاتحة كبر وأعاد القراءة لزوماً لأن القراءة إذا لم تتم كان امتناعاً عن الإتمام لا رفضاً للفرض . ولو تحول رأيه بعدما صلى ركعة وكبر بالقول الثاني، فإن تحول إلى قول ابن عباس بعدما كبر بقول ابن مسعود وقرأ إن لم يفرغ من القراءة يكبر ما بقي من تكبيرات ابن عباس ويعيد القراءة، وإن فرغ من القراءة كبر ما بقي ولا يعيد القراءة
His statement (and he should make the two recitations consecutive) following Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, and so that the takbirs are gathered, because they are among the symbols of the Shari'ah, and therefore vocalizing them is obligatory, and gathering achieves the meaning of rituals and announcement. However, in the first rak'ah, the extra (takbirs) intervene between the opening takbir and the takbir of ruku', so it is obligatory to attach them to the opening takbir because it comes first. In the second rak'ah, the basis is the takbir of ruku' and nothing else, so it is obligatory to attach them to it by necessity. Thus in al-Muhit and al-Hidayah. And it appears that by 'obligatory' in their expressions they mean established, not the technical term, because making them consecutive is recommended, as previously mentioned that the difference is about preference. Then, the latecomer who missed one rak'ah, when he stands to make up, he should recite first and then make takbir, because if he starts with takbir, he would be making the takbirs consecutive (one after another) and no one among the Companions said that. If he starts with recitation, his action agrees with the saying of Ali, so it is more appropriate. Thus in al-Muhit, and it specifies their saying that the latecomer makes up the first part of his prayer with regard to dhikrs, and the latecomer makes takbir according to his own opinion, unlike the one who catches up later (lahiq) because he is behind the imam in ruling. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Mujtaba: The principle is that whoever advances the delayed or delays the advanced forgetfully or by ijtihad, if he has not finished what he has entered into, he repeats, and if he has finished, he does not return (to correct it). In al-Muhit: If the imam starts with recitation forgetfully and then remembers, if he has finished reciting al-Fatihah and the surah, he continues his prayer; if he has only recited al-Fatihah, he makes takbir and repeats the recitation as a matter of necessity, because the recitation, if not completed, is a cessation from completion, not a rejection of the obligatory. If his opinion changes after he has prayed one rak'ah and made takbir according to the second opinion, then if he changes to the opinion of Ibn Abbas after having made takbir according to the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud and recited, if he has not finished the recitation, he makes the remaining takbirs of Ibn Abbas and repeats the recitation; if he has finished the recitation, he makes the remaining takbirs and does not repeat the recitation.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage explains the proper sequence of takbirs and recitation in the Eid prayer. It begins by stating that the two recitations (in the two rak'ahs) should be consecutive (muwalat) to follow the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and to gather the takbirs as a symbol of Islam. The reason for joining the extra takbirs to the nearest obligatory takbir differs between the first and second rak'ah. In the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs are attached to the opening takbir because they occur between it and the ruku' takbir; in the second, they are attached to the ruku' takbir because that is the next obligatory takbir after the opening. The commentator notes that 'obligatory' here means 'established' (thubut) rather than the technical wajib, as the actual ruling is recommendation. Then it addresses the latecomer who missed one rak'ah: when he stands to make up the missed rak'ah, he should recite first (after the opening takbir) and then make the extra takbirs, because starting with takbirs would make the takbirs consecutive without anything between, which is not reported from the Companions. This is also the opinion of Ali. The passage also covers cases of forgetfulness or ijtihad by the imam, and the case of changing one's opinion (taḥawwul al-ra'y) regarding which set of takbirs to follow.

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalat): The consecutive order between the two recitations in the two rak'ahs of Eid prayer.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): One who joins the prayer late but after the imam has already started; distinguished from the masbuq.
تحول الرأي (tahawwul al-ra'y): Change of ijtihad regarding the number of takbirs during the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a latecomer (masbuq) who missed one rak'ah of Eid prayer do when standing to make it up?
A) Make extra takbirs first, then recite.
B) Recite first, then make extra takbirs.
C) Omit extra takbirs.
D) Recite and make takbirs simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
In Eid prayer, the extra takbirs are attached to the nearest obligatory takbir, and the latecomer must recite first then make takbir to follow the Sunnah.

Raising Hands During Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer
Ruling on raising hands during the extra takbirs and the exception for the latecomer in ruku'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the extra takbirs in Eid prayer, identify the exception for the latecomer in ruku', and apply the flexible silence measure between takbirs.

Core Idea
Raise hands during the extra Eid takbirs; the pause between them varies with the crowd.

The Eid prayer includes extra takbirs called al-zawa'id. A common practical question is whether to raise the hands during these takbirs, and for how long to pause. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that raising hands is a sunnah, not for the ruku' takbirs, and that the silence between takbirs is a flexible measure to avoid confusion. It also addresses the special case of a latecomer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act (raising hands during extra takbirs) and its hukm level (sunnah, not wajib).
2
Distinguish from the ruku' takbirs
Note that the ruling does not apply to the takbirs of ruku', even though they are considered wajib like the extra takbirs.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify the weak transmission from Abu Yusuf that hands are not raised, and that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) is to raise them.
4
Apply the exception for the latecomer
Understand that a latecomer who makes takbir while bowing does not raise his hands, according to al-Usbijabi.
5
Apply the silence measure flexibly
The silence between takbirs is estimated at three tasbihat but is not binding; it varies with the size of the crowd to remove ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويرفع يديه في الزوائد) توضيح لما أبهمه سابقاً بقوله : ولا يرفع الأيدي إلا في «فقعس صمعج». فإن العين الأولى للإشارة إلى العيدين فبين هنا أنه خاص بالزوائد دون تكبيرة الركوع فإن تكبيرتي الركوع لما ألحقت بالزوائد في كونهما واجبتين حتى يجب السهو بتركهما ساهياً كما صرح به في الزوائد ويستثنى منه ما إذا كبر راكعا لكونه مسبوقاً كما قدمناه فإنه لا يرفع يديه كما ذكره الأسبيجابي . وقيل : يرفع يديه. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يسكت بين كل تكبيرتين لأنه ليس بينهما ذكر مسنون عندنا، ولهذا يرسل يديه عندنا وقدره مقدار ثلاث تسبيحات لزوال الاشتباه. وذكر في المبسوط أن هذا التقدير ليس بلازم بل يختلف بكثرة الزحام وقلته لأن المقصود إزالة الاشتباه، ولم يذكر هنا الجهر بالقراءة لما علم سابقاً في فضل القراءة ويقرأ فيهما كما يقرأ في الجمعة. وفي الظهيرية : لو صلى خلف إمام لا يرى رفع اليدين عند تكبيرات الزوائد يرفع يديه ولا يوافق الإمام في الترك اهـ .
قوله : (فإن تكبيرتي الركوع الخ) ظاهره أن تكبيرة الركوع في الركعتين واجب يجب بتركه سجود السهو وهكذا فهمه في الشرنبلالية من عبارة المؤلف فاعترضه بأن الكمال صرح في باب سجود السهو بأنه لا يجب بترك تكبيرات الانتقال إلا في تكبيرة ركوع الركعة الثانية من صلاة العيد اهـ . قلت : والمؤلف أيضاً صرح بذلك هناك فيتعين حمل كلامه هنا على أن المراد بتكبيرتي الركوع التكبيرتان في ركوعي الركعة الثانية من صلاتي العيدين وهذا وإن كان فيه نوع بعد لكنه يرتكب توفيقاً بين كلاميه .
His statement (and he raises his hands in the extra takbirs) is an explanation of what he previously left ambiguous by his statement: 'He does not raise hands except in...' [unclear]. For the first letter points to the two Eids, so he clarifies here that it is specific to the extra takbirs, not the takbir of ruku', because the two takbirs of ruku' are attached to the extra takbirs in that they are obligatory, such that forgetfulness prostration is required for leaving them forgetfully, as stated in al-Zawa'id. An exception is made for the case where he makes takbir while bowing because he is a latecomer, as we have mentioned: he does not raise his hands, as mentioned by al-Usbijabi. And it is said: he raises his hands. The author indicated that he remains silent between every two takbirs because there is no sunnah dhikr between them according to us, and therefore he lets his hands hang down according to us, and its measure is the duration of three tasbihat to remove ambiguity. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that this measure is not binding but varies with the abundance or scarcity of the crowd because the purpose is to remove ambiguity. He did not mention here the loud recitation because it was previously known in the section on the virtue of recitation, and he recites in them as he recites in Jumu'ah. In al-Zahiriyyah: If he prays behind an imam who does not believe in raising hands during the extra takbirs, he raises his hands and does not follow the imam in leaving it. End.

His statement: (For the two takbirs of ruku'...) Its apparent meaning is that the takbir of ruku' in the two rak'ahs is obligatory, and leaving it forgetfully requires prostration of forgetfulness. Thus it was understood in al-Shurnubalaliyyah from the author's expression, but he objected that al-Kamal stated in the chapter on prostration of forgetfulness that leaving the takbirs of transition does not require prostration except for the takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of the Eid prayer. I say: The author also stated that there, so his words here must be interpreted to mean that by 'the two takbirs of ruku'' he means the two takbirs in the ruku' of the second rak'ah of the two Eid prayers. Although this is somewhat forced, it is adopted to reconcile his two statements.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on raising the hands during the extra takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id) in the Eid prayer. It specifies that the earlier ambiguous statement refers only to the extra takbirs, not to the takbirs of ruku'. The two takbirs of ruku' are likened to the extra takbirs in being obligatory such that forgetting them requires prostration of forgetfulness, but they are not included in the ruling of raising hands. An exception is made for the latecomer who makes takbir while in ruku': according to al-Usbijabi, he does not raise his hands, though there is a contrary opinion. The author also discusses the silence between takbirs, which should last approximately three tasbihat, though this varies with the crowd. The passage ends with a significant marginal note that resolves an apparent contradiction in the author's statements about whether the two takbirs of ruku' require prostration of forgetfulness. The note explains that the 'two takbirs of ruku'' refer specifically to the takbirs of the second rak'ah of the two Eid prayers, thus harmonizing the texts.

Key Terms
الزوائد (al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs in Eid prayer beyond the opening takbir and the ruku' takbirs.
تكبيرات الركوع (takbirat al-rukūʿ): The takbirs said when going into ruku' in each rak'ah.
السكوت بين التكبيرتين (al-sukut bayn al-takbiratain): The silence between the extra takbirs, estimated at three tasbihat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is recommended (sunnah), and if the imam does not raise hands, the follower should still raise hands.
C) It is only for the imam, not the followers.
D) It is done only in the first rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Raising the hands during the extra takbirs of Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah, and the silence between them is flexible, varying with the crowd to remove confusion.

The Eid Sermon: Timing, Content, and Listening Obligation
Ruling on the timing and content of the Eid sermon and the obligation to listen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the Eid sermon relative to the prayer, identify the recommended and obligatory elements of the sermon content, and explain the consequence of not listening.

Core Idea
The Eid sermon is sunnah, not a condition, so it is after prayer; listening is wajib.

In the Hanafi school, the Eid sermon differs significantly from the Friday sermon. While the Friday sermon is a condition (shart) for the validity of the prayer and must precede it, the Eid sermon is a sunnah that follows the prayer. This lesson examines the precise timing, the recommended content (takbirs), and the obligation of the congregation to listen attentively. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between the two similar but legally distinct acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid sermon (khutbat al-'idayn). Determine its legal classification: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? The text states it is sunnah, following the Prophet's action.
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the Prophet's practice (fi'l): 'اقتداء بفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام' (following his action). This sunnah fi'liyyah is the basis for the timing and content.
No specific hadith text is quoted; the authority is the established practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The Prophet always delivered the Eid sermon after the prayer, establishing the normative practice. In contrast, the Friday sermon is before because it is a condition (shart) for the prayer. Since the Eid sermon is not a condition, it can be before, but that contradicts the sunnah.
If done before, the prayer is valid but the act is makruh (disliked).
4
Examine the sermon content and congregation's duty
The text from al-Mujtaba specifies that the Eid sermon begins with takbirs (nine in the first, seven in the second) and the imam makes fourteen takbirs before descending. The congregation must be silent and listen (wajib).
Listening is wajib, not just recommended.
5
Synthesise the practical consequence (thamarah)
The practical consequence: if someone does not listen, he commits a sin (since listening is wajib), but the prayer itself remains valid because the sermon is not a condition. The sermon is a sunnah act performed after the prayer.
This contrasts with Jumu'ah where the sermon is a condition and missing it invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويخطب بعدها خطبتين اقتداء بفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام بخلاف الجمعة فإنه يخطب قبلها لأن الخطبة فيها شرط والشرط متقدم أو مقارن وفي العيد ليست بشرط، ولهذا إذا خطب قبلها صح وكره لأنه خالف السنة كما لو تركها أصلاً. وفي المجتبى : ويبدأ بالتحميد في خطبة الجمعة وخطبة الاستسقاء وخطبة النكاح ، ويبدأ بالتكبيرات في خطبة العيدين، ويستحب أن يستفتح الأولى بتسع تكبيرات تترى، الله بن عتبة بن مسعود : هو والثانية بسبع . السنة. ويكبر قبل أن ينزل من المنبر أربع عشرة .اهـ. ويجب السكوت والاستماع في خطبة العيدين وخطبة الموسم كذا في المجتبى قوله ( ويعلم الناس فيها أحكام صدقة الفطر) لأنها شرعت لأجله. وقال في السراج الوهاج وأحكامها خمسة على من تجب ولمن تجب ومتى تجب وكم تجب ومم تجب. أما على من تجب فعلى الحر المسلم المالك للنصاب، وأما لمن تجب فللفقراء والمساكين، وأما متى تجب فبطلوع الفجر، وأما كم تجب فنصف صاع من برأ وصاع من تمر أو شعير أو زبيب، وأما مم تجب فمن أربعة أشياء المذكورة وأما ما سواها فبالقيمة قوله (ولم تقض إن فاتت مع الإمام لأن الصلاة بهذه الصفة لم تعرف قربة إلا بشرائط لا تتم بالمنفرد فمراده نفي صلاتها وحده وإلا فإذا فاتت مع إمام وأمكنه أن يذهب إلى إمام آخر فإنه يذهب إليه لأنه يجوز تعدادها في مصر واحد في موضعين وأكثر اتفاقاً إنما الخلاف في الجمعة. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا في الوقت أو خرج الوقت وما إذا لم يدخل مع الإمام أصلاً أو دخل معه وأفسدها فلا
His statement (and he delivers two sermons after it) following his action, peace be upon him, contrary to Friday, for the sermon is before it because the sermon is a condition (for Friday) and the condition is prior or simultaneous, while in Eid it is not a condition; therefore if he delivers it before, it is valid but disliked because he opposes the Sunnah, as if he left it entirely. In al-Mujtaba: He begins with praise (tahmid) in the Friday sermon, the rain sermon, and the marriage sermon, and begins with takbirs in the Eid sermon, and it is recommended to open the first with nine consecutive takbirs, and the second with seven. And he makes fourteen takbirs before descending from the pulpit. It is obligatory to be silent and listen in the Eid sermon and the sermon of the season (minaret sermon) as stated in al-Mujtaba. His statement (and he teaches the people in it the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr) because it was prescribed for it. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Its rulings are five: on whom it is obligatory, for whom it is given, when it is obligatory, how much it is, and from what it is given. As for on whom it is obligatory: upon the free Muslim who owns the nisab. As for for whom it is given: to the poor and needy. As for when it is obligatory: at the break of dawn. As for how much: half a sa' of wheat, and a sa' of dates, barley, or raisins. As for from what it is given: from the four mentioned items; if from other than these, then by value. His statement (and it is not made up if missed with the imam) because the prayer in this manner is not known as an act of worship except with conditions that cannot be fulfilled by one alone; so his intent is to negate performing it alone. Otherwise, if it is missed with one imam and it is possible to go to another imam, he goes to him, because it is permissible to have multiple congregations in one city in two or more places by agreement; the difference is only in Friday prayer. He made it absolute, so it includes whether it is within the time or after the time, and whether he did not enter with the imam at all or entered with him and invalidated it.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings related to the Eid sermon (khutbah). It begins by noting that the Eid sermon is delivered after the prayer, unlike the Friday sermon which precedes the prayer. This is because the sermon is a condition (shart) for Friday prayer but not for Eid; if one gives the sermon before the Eid prayer, it is valid but disliked. Then it discusses the content of the sermon: it should begin with takbirs (nine in the first, seven in the second), and the imam makes additional takbirs before descending from the pulpit. The congregation must listen attentively. The passage also emphasizes that during the sermon, the imam should teach the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr, summarizing its five key aspects: on whom it is obligatory (free Muslim possessing nisab), to whom it is given (poor and needy), when it becomes obligatory (dawn of Eid day), how much (half sa' of wheat or a sa' of other items), and from what commodities (the four mentioned, or value for others). Finally, it addresses the question of making up the missed Eid prayer. If one misses it with the imam, he does not pray it alone, because the congregational form with the specific conditions cannot be replicated individually. However, if another congregation is available, he should join it, as multiple Eid congregations in one city are permissible by consensus.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered during the Eid prayer, after the prayer itself.
السكوت والاستماع (al-sukut wa al-istima'): Silence and listening – the required attitude of the congregation during the sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on delivering the Eid sermon before the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the act is disliked (makruh).
C) The sermon is still valid but the prayer is invalid.
D) The sermon is invalid and must be repeated after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Eid sermon is a sunnah, not a condition; it is delivered after the prayer, and listening is wajib.

The Missed Eid Prayer and Teaching Sadaqat al-Fitr
Ruling on the missed Eid prayer and the obligation to teach sadaqat al-fitr during the sermon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the missed Eid prayer is not made up individually and list the five essential rulings of sadaqat al-fitr as taught in the Eid sermon.

Core Idea
Missed Eid prayer is not prayed alone; the congregation can be repeated; sadaqat al-fitr has five specific rulin gs taught in the sermon.

The Eid sermon is not just about praising Allah; the imam is also obligated to teach the congregation the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. The text from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj outlines five key questions: on whom it is obligatory, for whom, when, how much, and from what items. Additionally, a common practical issue arises when someone misses the Eid prayer with the imam. The Hanafi school rules that it is not to be made up alone, because the specific congregational form of the Eid prayer is not recognized as a valid act of worship for an individual. However, if another congregation is available, one should join it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject: teaching sadaqat al-fitr in the sermon
The text states that the imam should teach the people the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr during the Eid sermon because the sermon was prescribed for that purpose. This is part of the content.
This is a sunnah and a teaching opportunity.
2
List the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr from the text
The text from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj specifies five aspects: (1) on whom it is obligatory (free Muslim possessing nisab), (2) for whom it is given (the poor), (3) when it becomes obligatory (dawn of Eid day), (4) how much (half sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates, barley, or raisins), and (5) from what items (the four mentioned; if other items, then by value).
Memorize these five categories for fiqh exams.
3
Identify the ruling on the missed Eid prayer
The text says: 'ولم تقض إن فاتت مع الإمام' – the Eid prayer is not made up if missed with the imam. The reason is that the prayer in this specific form (with the extra takbirs and congregation) is not known as an act of worship (قربة) performed alone.
This is a distinctive Hanafi ruling.
4
Analyze the exceptions and details
The author clarifies that if the Eid prayer is missed with one imam, but another congregation is available in the same city, one should go to that other congregation. This is because multiple Eid congregations are permissible in one city by consensus, unlike Jumu'ah where there is a difference.
The ruling applies whether one missed the entire prayer or entered and then invalidated it.
5
Synthesize the practical scenario
A person who comes late to the Eid prayer and misses it entirely: he cannot pray it alone. He should search for another congregation. If none is available, the prayer is simply missed; there is no qada'.
This contrasts with a missed fard prayer which must be made up.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before the Eid prayer.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its time has passed.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes one liable for sadaqat al-fitr.

Checkpoint

A) He must pray two rak'ahs alone as a substitute.
B) He does not pray it; it is simply missed with no qada'.
C) He should pray two rak'ahs with extra takbirs alone.
D) He must go to another city to find a congregation.

Key Takeaway
Missed Eid prayer is not made up alone; one joins another congregation if possible; otherwise, it is not prayed at all. The sermon must include teaching the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr.

Raising Hands During Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer: Hanafi Position
Hanafi ruling on extra takbirs with intra-school difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during extra takbirs in Eid prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf's weak narration.

Core Idea
Raise hands for each extra takbir in Eid; the contrary narration is weak and not followed.

This passage addresses the specific ruling on raising hands during the extra takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id) in Eid prayer. While there is an intra-Hanafi dispute—Abu Yusuf reportedly held that hands should not be raised—the relied-upon position is that hands are raised for each extra takbir. This practice is based on the established sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions. The passage also clarifies that the follower should raise hands even if the imam does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising hands during the extra takbirs in Eid prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah); omitting it is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the general practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions, transmitted by reliable narrators. The passage cites no specific hadith but relies on this transmitted practice.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf narrated that hands should not be raised. The author explicitly calls this narration weak (da'if).
4
Explain the Hanafi tarjih
The author and the majority of Hanafi scholars (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) prefer raising hands. The weak narration from Abu Yusuf is not relied upon.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the imam does not raise his hands, the follower should still raise his hands, as the imam's omission does not override the established sunnah.
This is explicitly stated in al-Zahiriyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الزوائد ويخطب بعدها خطبتين يعلم فيهما أحكام صدقة الفطر ولم تقض إن فاتت مع السراج الوهاج، ربما توهم أنهما التحقنا بهما في الرفع أيضاً فنص على أنه خاص بالزوائد. وعن أبي يوسف : لا يرفع يديه فيها وهو ضعيف، ويستثنى منه ما إذا كبر راكعا لكونه مسبوقاً كما قدمناه فإنه لا يرفع يديه كما ذكره الأسبيجابي . وقيل : يرفع يديه. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يسكت بين كل تكبيرتين لأنه ليس بينهما ذكر مسنون عندنا، ولهذا يرسل يديه عندنا وقدره مقدار ثلاث تسبيحات لزوال الاشتباه. وذكر في المبسوط أن هذا التقدير ليس بلازم بل يختلف بكثرة الزحام وقلته لأن المقصود إزالة الاشتباه، ولم يذكر هنا الجهر بالقراءة لما علم سابقاً في فضل القراءة ويقرأ فيهما كما يقرأ في الجمعة. وفي الظهيرية : لو صلى خلف إمام لا يرى رفع اليدين عند تكبيرات الزوائد يرفع يديه ولا يوافق الإمام في الترك اهـ .
The extra takbirs and he delivers two sermons after them in which he teaches the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr, and it is not made up if missed with the imam. (The commentary): Perhaps one might think that the two sermons are also included in raising hands, so he specifies that it is specific to the extra takbirs. And from Abu Yusuf: he does not raise his hands in them, and it is weak. An exception is made for when he says takbir while bowing because he is a latecomer, as we have mentioned, for he does not raise his hands, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And it is said: he raises his hands. The author indicated that he remains silent between every two takbirs because there is no prescribed dhikr between them according to us, and therefore he lets his hands hang according to us, and its duration is the amount of three tasbihat to remove confusion. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that this estimation is not necessary but varies with the abundance or scarcity of crowding because the purpose is to remove confusion. He did not mention here raising the voice in recitation because it is known previously in the virtue of recitation, and he recites in them as he recites in Jumu'ah. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he prays behind an imam who does not view raising hands at the extra takbirs, he raises his hands and does not follow the imam in leaving it. End.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding raising hands during the extra takbirs (takbirat al-zawa'id) in Eid prayer. The author clarifies that the extra takbirs are the occasion for raising hands, not the sermons. The narration from Abu Yusuf that hands are not raised is considered weak. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that hands are raised for each extra takbir, following the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. An exception is made for a latecomer who says takbir while bowing—he does not raise his hands. The silent pause between takbirs is estimated by the time of three tasbihat, though this varies with crowding. If one follows an imam who does not raise hands, the follower should still raise hands, as the takbirs are a sunnah that the imam's omission does not override.

Key Terms
الزوائد (al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs in Eid prayer beyond the regular takbirat al-ihram and takbir al-ruk'u.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs recited in Eid prayer, specific to this occasion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what should a follower do if his imam does not raise his hands during the extra takbirs of Eid prayer?
A) The follower should not raise his hands to avoid differing from the imam.
B) The follower should raise his hands, as the imam's omission does not override the sunnah.
C) The follower should leave the congregation and pray alone.
D) The follower should repeat the prayer after the imam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, raise hands for each extra takbir in Eid; the contrary narration is weak and not followed.

The Eid Sermon: Timing, Structure, and the Five Rulings of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Explanation of the two sermons after Eid prayer and their content regarding sadaqat al-fitr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing and structure of the Eid sermon, identify the recommended takbirs, and explain the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr as taught in the sermon.

Core Idea
The Eid sermon is a sunnah after prayer, not before, and includes nine takbirs in the first and seven in the second, while teaching the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the unique fiqh of the Eid sermon. Unlike Jumu'ah, where the sermon is a condition before prayer, the Eid sermon is a sunnah after prayer. The sermon begins with takbirs, and it is recommended to teach the congregation the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr. We will explore the five key rulings that should be conveyed and the sunan of the sermon itself.

Guided Path
1
Compare with Jumu'ah
Identify that in Jumu'ah the sermon is a condition (shart) and therefore precedes the prayer, whereas in Eid it is a sunnah and comes after the prayer. This is the first key distinction.
The passage explicitly contrasts the two: 'بخلاف الجمعة فإنه يخطب قبلها لأن الخطبة فيها شرط'
2
List the sunan of the sermon
From the text, extract the recommended acts: opening with takbirs (9 in first, 7 in second, total 14 before descending), sitting between two sermons, and teaching sadaqat al-fitr rulings.
The takbir numbers are from al-Mujtaba, indicating consistency across reliable Hanafi sources.
3
Identify obligations on listeners
Note that silence and attentiveness (السكوت والاستماع) are obligatory (واجب) during the Eid sermon, as stated in al-Mujtaba.
This mirrors the obligation in Jumu'ah, showing the same etiquettes apply.
4
Extract the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr
Use the five questions from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: upon whom, for whom, when, how much, and from what. This is the content to be taught.
The passage gives the Hanafi answers: nisab condition, poor recipients, dawn of Eid day, half sa' of wheat or a sa' of other staples, and the specific grains or value.
5
Recognize the authority chain
The rulings are attributed to al-Mujtaba and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, two authoritative Hanafi texts. The proof for the timing is the Prophet's action (اقتداء بفعله).
Knowing the authority level (zahir al-riwayah) helps assess reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويخطب بعدها (خطبتين اقتداء بفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام بخلاف الجمعة فإنه يخطب قبلها لأن الخطبة فيها شرط والشرط متقدم أو مقارن وفي العيد ليست بشرط، ولهذا إذا خطب قبلها صح وكره لأنه خالف السنة كما لو تركها أصلاً. وفي المجتبى : ويبدأ بالتحميد في خطبة الجمعة وخطبة الاستسقاء وخطبة النكاح ، ويبدأ بالتكبيرات في خطبة العيدين، ويستحب أن يستفتح الأولى بتسع تكبيرات تترى، والثانية بسبع. ويكبر قبل أن ينزل من المنبر أربع عشرة .اهـ. ويجب السكوت والاستماع في خطبة العيدين وخطبة الموسم كذا في المجتبى قوله ( ويعلم الناس فيها أحكام صدقة الفطر) لأنها شرعت لأجله. وقال في السراج الوهاج وأحكامها خمسة على من تجب ولمن تجب ومتى تجب وكم تجب ومم تجب. أما على من تجب فعلى الحر المسلم المالك للنصاب، وأما لمن تجب فللفقراء والمساكين، وأما متى تجب فبطلوع الفجر، وأما كم تجب فنصف صاع من برأ وصاع من تمر أو شعير أو زبيب، وأما مم تجب فمن أربعة أشياء المذكورة وأما ما سواها فبالقيمة
His statement (and he delivers two sermons after them) following his action, peace be upon him, contrary to Jumu'ah where he delivers sermons before it because the sermon is a condition there, and the condition precedes or is concurrent. In Eid it is not a condition, and hence if he delivers the sermon before it, it is valid but disliked because it contradicts the Sunnah, just as if he leaves it entirely. In al-Mujtaba: He begins with praise in the Jumu'ah sermon, the istisqa sermon, and the marriage sermon, and he begins with takbirs in the Eid sermons. It is recommended to open the first with nine consecutive takbirs, and the second with seven. He says takbir fourteen times before descending from the minbar. End. And it is obligatory to remain silent and listen in the Eid sermons and the season sermon, as in al-Mujtaba. His statement (and teaches the people therein the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr) because it was prescribed for its sake. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Its rulings are five: upon whom it is obligatory, for whom it is obligatory, when it is obligatory, how much is obligatory, and from what it is obligatory. As for upon whom it is obligatory: upon the free Muslim who owns a nisab. As for for whom it is obligatory: for the poor and needy. As for when it is obligatory: at the break of dawn. As for how much is obligatory: half a sa' of wheat, a sa' of dates, barley, or raisins. As for from what it is obligatory: from the four mentioned items; as for other than them, by value.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling explaining the nature and content of the Eid sermons. The author establishes that unlike Jumu'ah, the Eid sermon is not a condition for the prayer's validity; it is a sunnah performed after the prayer. The sermon begins with takbirs rather than tahmid. It is recommended to say nine takbirs in the first sermon and seven in the second. The sermon should include teachings about sadaqat al-fitr (zakat al-fitr), covering five key aspects: on whom it is obligatory (free Muslim possessing nisab), for whom (the poor), when (dawn of Eid day), how much (half sa' of wheat or one sa' of other staples), and from what items (the four specified grains or their value). The listener is required to remain silent and listen attentively.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, before Eid prayer, to purify the fast and provide for the needy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the timing of the Eid sermon?
A) It must be delivered before the Eid prayer.
B) It must be delivered after the Eid prayer.
C) It can be delivered either before or after without dislike.
D) No sermon is required for Eid.

Key Takeaway
The Eid sermon is a sunnah after the prayer, not a condition, and it is recommended to teach the five rulings of sadaqat al-fitr during it.

Ruling on Making Up Eid Prayer Missed with Imam
Hanafi ruling on qada and repetition of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of Eid prayer and apply it to scenarios of missing or invalidating it.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is not made up individually because its conditions require congregation; join another imam or pray Duha.

Eid prayer is a wajib congregational act. What happens when you miss it? The Hanafi school has a clear answer: the prayer cannot be performed alone because its special conditions require congregation. However, you are encouraged to join another congregation or, if that is not possible, to pray a voluntary prayer to seek reward. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning, and an important difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
Eid prayer is wajib upon eligible Muslims (male, free, resident). Understand that it is not a nafl or fard but a wajib.
Wajib means obligatory but proof is zanni.
2
Understand the question: what if missed?
The passage addresses whether qada (make-up) is required when one misses the Eid prayer with the imam, either completely or after starting.
It also covers invalidation during the prayer.
3
Trace the main reasoning
The prayer in this special form (with extra takbirs, congregation) is not known as a valid act of worship except with conditions that an individual cannot fulfill alone. Hence, no qada alone.
However, if another congregation is available, one should join it.
4
Analyze the two scenarios: within time vs. out of time
If invalidated intentionally (e.g., breaking wudu) while time remains, repeat it with congregation if possible. If time expires, the obligation falls and no qada, but one may pray four rak'ahs like Duha.
This is by analogy with Jumu'ah.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that starting makes it like a vow, requiring qada if invalidated. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) reject this. The relied-upon view is the majority.
The mufta bihi is no qada after time; Duha is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولم تقض إن فاتت مع الإمام لأن الصلاة بهذه الصفة لم تعرف قربة إلا بشرائط لا تتم بالمنفرد فمراده نفي صلاتها وحده وإلا فإذا فاتت مع إمام وأمكنه أن يذهب إلى إمام آخر فإنه يذهب إليه لأنه يجوز تعدادها في مصر واحد في موضعين وأكثر اتفاقاً إنما الخلاف في الجمعة. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا في الوقت أو خرج الوقت وما إذا لم يدخل مع الإمام أصلاً أو دخل معه وأفسدها فلا قضاء عليه أصلاً. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أفسدها بعد الشروع يقضي لأن الشروع في الإيجاب كالنذر. كذا في المحيط . ولا يخفى أنه إذا لم يلزمه القضاء فالإثم عليه لترك الواجب من غير عذر كالسجدة الصلاتية إذا لم يسجد لها حتى فرغ من صلاته. وفي البدائع : وأما حكمها إذا فسدت أو فاتت فكل ما يفسد سائر الصلوات والجمعة يفسدها من خروج الوقت ولو بعد القعود وفوت الجماعة على التفصيل والاختلاف المذكور في الجمعة غير أنها إن فسدت بنحو حدث عمد يستقبلها، وإن فسدت بخروج الوقت سقطت ولا يقضيها عندنا كالجمعة ولكنه يصلي أربعاً مثل صلاة الضحى إن شاء لأنها إذا فاتته لا يمكن تداركها بالقضاء لفقد الشرائط ، فلو صلى مثل الضحي لنيل الثواب كان حسناً وهو مروي عن ابن مسعود.
His statement (and it is not made up if missed with the imam) because the prayer in this manner is not known as an act of worship except with conditions that are not fulfilled by an individual. So his intent is to negate praying it alone; otherwise, if one missed it with one imam and it is possible to go to another imam, he goes to it because it is permissible to have multiple congregations in one city in two or more places, by agreement; the dispute is only regarding Jumu'ah. And his statement is absolute, covering whether it is within the time or out of time, and whether one did not join the imam at all or joined and invalidated it; there is no qada upon him at all. Abu Yusuf said: If he invalidates it after commencing, he makes it up because commencement makes it obligatory like a vow. This is in al-Muhit. It is not hidden that if qada is not incumbent upon him, he is sinful for leaving a wajib without excuse, like the sajda of prayer if one does not perform it until after finishing his prayer. In al-Bada'i: As for its ruling if it is invalidated or missed, everything that invalidates other prayers and Jumu'ah invalidates it, such as leaving of time even after sitting, and missing the congregation, according to the detail and difference mentioned in Jumu'ah, except that if it is invalidated by something like intentional hadath, he repeats it; if invalidated by leaving of time, it falls away and he does not make it up according to us, like Jumu'ah, but he prays four rak'ahs like the Duha prayer if he wishes, because if it is missed, it cannot be made up due to loss of conditions. So if he prays like Duha to attain reward, it is good, and it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the qada (make-up) of Eid prayer. The Hanafi position is that Eid prayer is not made up individually if missed because its congregational character is essential. If one misses it with one imam but can attend another congregation, he should go to that other imam. If it is invalidated intentionally (e.g., by breaking wudu), one repeats it within the time. If the time passes, there is no qada, but one may pray four rak'ahs as nafl like Duha to seek reward. Abu Yusuf holds that if one starts and then invalidates, qada is required like a vow, but the majority (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagree. The sin of missing it without excuse remains, like neglecting a wajib.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person misses Eid prayer with the imam entirely (did not start), what should he do?
A) He must make it up as qada at home.
B) He should join another Eid congregation if possible; otherwise, no qada.
C) He prays two rak'ahs alone with extra takbirs.
D) He does nothing and it is not sinful.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is not made up individually; join another congregation if possible, otherwise pray nafl Duha.

Takbirat al-Ruk'u in the Second Raka'at of Eid Prayer
Critical refinement of a ruling on takbirs in Eid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which takbir in Eid prayer is wajib and apply the reconciliation method to apparent contradictions in Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Only the takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer is wajib; omission requires sajda sahw.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced point regarding the takbirs in Eid prayer. The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies an apparent contradiction in his own text, confirming that the obligation to perform sajda sahw for omitting a transition takbir applies only to the ruku' takbir of the second rak'ah. This reconciliation is a fine example of the interpretive skill required in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Recognize that the author initially says 'two takbirs of ruku'' implying both rak'ahs, but later states only the second rak'ah's takbir is wajib.
2
Locate the two statements
One statement is from the chapter on Eid; the other from the chapter on sajda sahw.
3
Apply the reconciliation (tawfiq)
Interpret 'two takbirs' as the two takbirs in the second rak'ah of the two Eid prayers (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha).
This resolves the contradiction without discarding either statement.
4
Derive the correct ruling
Conclude that only the takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah is wajib; omission requires sajda sahw. All other transition takbirs are sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن تكبيرتي الركوع الخ) ظاهره أن تكبيرة الركوع في الركعتين واجب يجب بتركه سجود السهو وهكذا فهمه في الشرنبلالية من عبارة المؤلف فاعترضه بأن الكمال صرح في باب سجود السهو بأنه لا يجب بترك تكبيرات الانتقال إلا في تكبيرة ركوع الركعة الثانية من صلاة العيد اهـ . قلت : والمؤلف أيضاً صرح بذلك هناك فيتعين حمل كلامه هنا على أن المراد بتكبيرتي الركوع التكبيرتان في ركوعي الركعة الثانية من صلاتي العيدين وهذا وإن كان فيه نوع بعد لكنه يرتكب توفيقاً بين كلاميه .
His statement: (For the two takbirs of ruku' etc.) Its apparent meaning is that the takbir of ruku' in both rak'ahs is obligatory; omitting it requires sajda sahw. Thus it was understood in al-Sharnablaliyyah from the author's expression. But he [al-Kamal] objected that al-Kamal explicitly stated in the chapter of sajda sahw that omitting the takbirs of transition does not require sajda except for the takbir of ruku' of the second rak'ah of Eid prayer. End. I say: The author also explicitly stated that there, so his words here must be interpreted to mean that by 'two takbirs of ruku'' he means the two takbirs in the ruku' of the second rak'ah of both Eid prayers. Though there is some distance [in this interpretation], it is adopted to reconcile his statements.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement resolving an apparent contradiction within the author's own work. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (and the commentator) discusses a statement from the original text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) regarding 'two takbirs of ruku'. Initially it seems the author says that the takbirs for ruku' in both rak'ahs are obligatory, requiring sajda sahw if omitted. However, in the chapter on sajda sahw, the same author explicitly states that only the takbir for ruku' in the second rak'ah of each Eid prayer is obligatory. To reconcile, the commentator interprets 'two takbirs of ruku'' to mean the two takbirs in the ruku' of the second rak'ah of the two Eid prayers (i.e., one for each Eid). This harmonizes the two statements.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required to compensate for omission or addition in prayer.
تكبيرات الانتقال (takbirat al-intiqal): Takbirs recited when moving between postures in prayer (e.g., bowing, prostrating).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, omitting which takbir in Eid prayer requires sajda sahw?
A) The takbir of ruku' in the first rak'ah.
B) The takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah.
C) All extra takbirs.
D) The opening takbir.

Key Takeaway
The takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer is wajib; omitting it requires sajda sahw. All other transition takbirs are sunnah.
