Delaying Eid Prayer Due to an Excuse
Hanafi ruling on making up missed Eid prayer due to excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up a missed Eid prayer and explain the condition of a valid excuse and its time limit.

Core Idea
Missed Eid prayer is made up the next day only, and only if there was an excuse.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific question: what happens if the Eid prayer is missed on its proper day? The Hanafi school, following Abu Yusuf, allows the prayer to be performed the next day, but only if there was a valid excuse. The author explains the legal principle and the proof from hadith, and also notes the difference of opinion with Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (Eid prayer) and the default rule: normally, the Eid prayer is not made up if missed, as stated at the beginning of the passage.
The principle is 'al-asl an la tuqda' (the default is that it is not made up).
2
Locate the exception: the hadith
Find the proof cited for the exception: the hadith of Anas where the Prophet ﷺ delayed the Eid prayer to the next day due to confusion about the moon.
This hadith overrides the general principle.
3
Understand the condition: excuse
Identify the condition that triggers the exception: a valid Shari'ah-recognized excuse (udhr). Without an excuse, the prayer is not made up.
Examples: ignorance of the date, heavy rain, fear.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa held the opposite view: no qada at all. Abu Yusuf allowed the next-day qada with excuse.
The text states this difference via al-Tahawi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Recognize that the relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's, because the hadith provides specific evidence. The author uses 'al-ibarah al-jayyidah' to indicate the preferred expression.
The mufta bihi: delay until noon of the next day with an excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتؤخر بعذر إلى الغد فقط لأن الأصل فيها أن لا تقضى لكن ورد الحديث بتأخيرها إلى الغد للعذر فبقي ما عداه على الأصل فلا تؤخر إلى الغد بغير عذر ولا إلى ما بعده بعذر. ولما قدم أن انتهاء وقته زوال الشمس من اليوم الأول لم يحتج إلى التقييد هنا، فالعبارة الجيدة وتؤخر بعذر إلى الزوال من الغد فقط». ولم يذكر في الكتب المعتبرة اختلاف في هذا، وذكر في المجتبى عن الطحاوي في شرح الآثار أن هذا قول أبي يوسف. وقال أبو حنيفة : إن فاتت في اليوم الأول لم تقض. لأبي يوسف حديث أنس قال: أخبرني عمومتي من الأنصار أن الهلال خفي على الناس في آخر ليلة من شهر رمضان فأصبحوا صياماً فشهدوا عند النبي الله بعد الزوال أنهم رأوا الهلال في الليلة الماضية فأمرهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالفطر فأفطروا، وخرج بهم من الغد فصلى بهم ... الحديث
His statement: (And it is delayed due to an excuse until the next day only) because the principle is that it is not made up, but the hadith came regarding delaying it to the next day due to an excuse, so other than that remains on the principle. Thus it is not delayed to the next day without an excuse, nor to beyond the next day with an excuse. Since he previously stated that its time ends at noon of the first day, there was no need for qualification here, so the good expression is 'and it is delayed due to an excuse until noon of the next day only.' No difference is mentioned in reliable books. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba from al-Tahawi in Sharh al-Athar that this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa said: If it is missed on the first day, it is not made up. For Abu Yusuf is the hadith of Anas: 'My uncles from the Ansar told me that the new moon was hidden from the people on the last night of Ramadan, so they woke up fasting. Then they testified before the Prophet ﷺ after noon that they had seen the moon the previous night, so the Prophet ﷺ ordered them to break their fast, and they did, and he went out with them the next day and prayed with them...'
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the postponement of Eid prayer due to an excuse. The Hanafi position (according to Abu Yusuf) allows delaying the Eid prayer to the next day until noon if there is a valid excuse (e.g., not knowing the date). The proof is the hadith of Anas where the Prophet ﷺ delayed the Eid prayer to the next day after a confusion about the moon. Abu Hanifa holds that if missed on the first day, it is not made up at all, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf due to the hadith. The delay is only to the next day, not beyond, and only with an excuse.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse such as ignorance of the date or inability to gather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position, till when can the Eid prayer be delayed if there is an excuse?
A) Until the end of the month of Shawwal.
B) Until noon of the next day.
C) Until the following Friday.
D) It cannot be delayed at all.

Key Takeaway
Missed Eid prayer is made up only the next day before noon, and only if there was a valid excuse; without excuse, it is not made up.
